The Synonymous Relationship Between Prophet and Messenger
Al-Ujhuri explains the synonymy of prophet and messenger with different references.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nuanced meanings of the terms 'prophet' (nabi) and 'messenger' (rasul) as explained by al-Ujhuri, including the grammatical discussion of ishar and idmar.

Core Idea
Prophet and messenger are synonymous in this context, but not perfectly interchangeable.

Al-Ujhuri begins by clarifying a key point in the matn: the claim that 'prophet' and 'messenger' are synonymous. He explains that this synonymy is relative to the specific meaning intended, whether that of a messenger or a prophet, and he addresses a subtle grammatical point about why the text uses explicit mention instead of implicit reference.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the full passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the two occurrences of the phrase 'mutaradifan' and how they are explained differently.
The passage references two external commentaries.
2
Identify the two interpretations of synonymy
The first interpretation says synonymous in the sense of 'rasul' (messenger). The second says synonymous in the sense of 'nabi' (prophet). Understand that the same word can have different references.
This shows that the matn's statement is not absolute.
3
Understand the grammatical point (ishar and idmar)
Al-Ujhuri mentions an objection: why is there an explicit mention where an implicit reference would suffice? He argues it's not a proper instance of ishar fi maqam al-idmar because it spans two sentences.
This is a minor linguistic technicality.
4
Review the key terms
Note the terms 'mutaradifan' (synonymous), 'ishar' (explicit mention), and 'idmar' (implicit reference). They are central to understanding the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري
:(قوله مُتَرَادِفَانِ) أي: على معنى الرسول كما في "شرح الشنشوري) على الرحبية". تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي.
ولك أن تمنع أن هنا إظهاراً في مقام الإضمار؛ لأنه لا يكون إلا في جملة واحدة، وما هنا ليس كذلك كما نُقِلَ عن الشَّبْرَامُلسِي.
(قوله: وَقِيلَ: إِنَّهُمَا مُتَرَادِفَانِ) أي: على معنى النبي السابق كما هو الظاهر.
(قوله: فَخَلِيفَةٌ) وقد اتَّصَفَ بها النبي الله أيضاً، وكانت بعده لأبي بكر، ثم لعُمَرَ، ثم لعثمان، ثم لعليّ، ولما توفّي علي بايع الناس لابنه الحسن، فصار خليفة حقاً مدة ستة أشهرٍ تكملة الثلاثين سنةً التي أَخْبَرَ النبي الله أنها مُدَّه الخلافة، ثم تكون ملكاً عضوضاً، أي: يَعُضُ الناسُ عنه لجَوْرِ أهله وعدم استقامتهم.
ولما فَرَغَتْ تلك المدَّةُ رَغِبَ عن الخلافة لمعاوية زُهْداً وصَوْناً لدماء المسلمين، فإنه بايعه أكثر من أربعين ألفاً، وهذا مِصْدَاقُ قوله : «وَلَعَلَّ اللهَ أَنْ يُصْلِحَ بِهِ بَيْنِ فِئَتَيْنِ عَظِيمَتَيْنِ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ» (۳).
The gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ujhuri: (His statement 'synonymous') means: in the sense of messenger (rasul) as in 'Sharh al-Shanshuri on al-Rahbiyya'. Annotations of the scholar Muhammad al-Anbabi. And you may object that here there is an ishar (making explicit) in place of idmar (implicitness); because it only occurs in one sentence, and here it is not like that as transmitted from al-Shabramulisi. (His statement 'and it was said: they are synonymous') means: in the sense of the previous prophet (nabi) as is apparent. (His statement 'then a caliph') — and the Prophet (peace be upon him) was also characterized with it, and after him it was for Abu Bakr, then for Umar, then for Uthman, then for Ali. And when Ali died, the people pledged allegiance to his son al-Hasan, so he became a caliph in truth for a period of six months, completing the thirty years which the Prophet (peace be upon him) informed were the duration of the caliphate, then it will become a biting kingdom, i.e., people will bite it because of the injustice of its people and their lack of uprightness. And when that period ended, he renounced the caliphate in favor of Muawiya out of asceticism and to protect the blood of Muslims, for more than forty thousand pledged to him, and this is the confirmation of his saying: 'Perhaps Allah will bring reconciliation between two great groups of Muslims through him.' (3)
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a gloss by Ahmad al-Ujhuri commenting on the matn of Sanusi. It begins by explaining the term 'mutaradifan' (synonymous) in the matn, stating that it means synonymous in the sense of 'rasul' (messenger), and references a commentary on al-Rahbiyya by al-Shanshuri. It then mentions a possible objection regarding the use of ishar (explicit mention) in place of idmar (implicit reference), but notes that this is not the case here. The gloss then clarifies that the second occurrence of 'they are synonymous' refers to the previous term 'nabi'. Finally, it discusses the term 'khalifa' from the matn, noting that the Prophet was also described as a caliph. It then provides a historical account of the caliphs after the Prophet: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali, and then al-Hasan for six months, completing the thirty-year caliphate predicted by the Prophet. After that, the caliphate becomes a 'biting kingdom' (mulk an 'adud) due to injustice. The gloss ends by mentioning that al-Hasan renounced the caliphate in favor of Muawiya to avoid bloodshed, and cites a hadith that this act might bring reconciliation.

Key Terms
مترادفان
إظهار
إضمار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophet and messenger are exactly the same in every context.
Correction: Al-Ujhuri shows they can be synonymous relative to a specific sense, but they are not always identical; the passage clarifies that the matn uses them interchangeably but with different emphases.

Checkpoint
According to the gloss, what does the first 'mutaradifan' mean?
A) Synonymous in the sense of messenger
B) Synonymous in the sense of prophet
C) Synonymous in the sense of caliph
D) Synonymous in the sense of king

Key Takeaway
The terms 'prophet' and 'messenger' can be used synonymously, but their precise reference depends on the context.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a seemingly redundant or explicit phrase in Islamic texts, do you tend to dismiss it as unnecessary, or do you pause to consider that the author may have a precise reason for the wording? How can you cultivate the same care as al-Ujhuri in your own reading of sacred texts?
?
The scholarly attention to grammatical detail in this passage shows that even a small nuance can affect the meaning of a theological statement. Is there an area of your beliefs where you have been satisfied with a vague understanding, assuming the details don't matter? What step will you take this week to seek precision in that area?

5 min
The Historical Caliphate and the Thirty-Year Prophecy
Al-Ujhuri lists the caliphs and explains the thirty-year caliphate prophecy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sequence of the caliphate after the Prophet Muhammad, the completion of thirty years as foretold, and the transition to a 'biting kingdom'.

Core Idea
The caliphate lasted exactly thirty years as promised, then became a monarchy.

Al-Ujhuri continues by explaining the term 'khalifa' from the matn, noting that even the Prophet was called a caliph. He then provides a historical list of the khalifas from Abu Bakr to al-Hasan, emphasizing that al-Hasan's six-month reign completed the prophesied thirty years. After that, the caliphate turned into a 'biting kingdom' due to injustice, and al-Hasan abdicated to Muawiya to prevent bloodshed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the caliphate
Read the second part of the gloss focusing on the caliphate. Notice the list of names and the specific mention of al-Hasan's six months.
The passage includes a hadith about reconciliation.
2
Identify the caliphs mentioned
List them in order: Prophet, Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali, al-Hasan. Understand that the Prophet is included as a caliph.
This list covers the 'rightly guided' caliphs and al-Hasan.
3
Understand the significance of thirty years
The Prophet said the caliphate would last thirty years. Al-Hasan's six months completed the thirty years after the earlier caliphs.
After that, the caliphate becomes a 'biting kingdom' (mulk 'adud).
4
Examine the abdication of al-Hasan
Al-Hasan renounced the caliphate to Muawiya to avoid bloodshed, fulfilling a hadith that Allah would bring reconciliation through him.
This shows the virtue of al-Hasan and the end of the prophetic caliphate.

(قوله: وَقِيلَ: إِنَّهُمَا مُتَرَادِفَانِ) أي: على معنى النبي السابق كما هو الظاهر.

It begins by explaining the term 'mutaradifan' (synonymous) in the matn, stating that it means synonymous in the sense of 'rasul' (messenger), and references a commentary on al-Rahbiyya by al-Shanshuri. It then mentions a possible objection regarding the use of ishar (explicit mention) in place of idmar (implicit reference), but notes that this is not the case here. The gloss then clarifies that the second occurrence of 'they are synonymous' refers to the previous term 'nabi'. Finally, it discusses the term 'khalifa' from the matn, noting that the Prophet was also described as a caliph. It then provides a historical account of the caliphs after the Prophet: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali, and then al-Hasan for six months, completing the thirty-year caliphate predicted by the Prophet. After that, the caliphate becomes a 'biting kingdom' (mulk an 'adud) due to injustice. The gloss ends by mentioning that al-Hasan renounced the caliphate in favor of Muawiya to avoid bloodshed, and cites a hadith that this act might bring reconciliation.

Key Terms
خليفة
ملك عضوض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The caliphate ended with the death of Ali or continued forever without change.
Correction: The gloss teaches that the prophetic caliphate lasted exactly thirty years including al-Hasan, after which it turned into a kingdom.

Checkpoint
According to the gloss, how long did al-Hasan's caliphate last?
A) Six months
B) One year
C) Thirty years
D) Until his death

Key Takeaway
The prophetic caliphate ended after thirty years with al-Hasan, after which it became a kingdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says al-Hasan renounced his legitimate caliphate to protect Muslim blood. When have you held onto a position or right that was causing division, even if you were in the right? What would it take for you to let go for the sake of unity?
?
The Prophet foretold that after thirty years the caliphate would become a 'biting kingdom.' In your own leadership—whether in your family, workplace, or community—can you identify a moment when you shifted from serving to ruling? How will you return to genuine service today?
?
Al-Hasan's abdication is described as an act of asceticism (zuhd). What worldly attachment are you clinging to that is harming your relationship with Allah or others? What step can you take this week to renounce it for a higher purpose?

Sufficiency of Any Prophet's Da'wa?
Al-Bajuri discusses whether da'wa of any prophet suffices and concludes ahl al-fatra are saved.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly debate about whose prophetic call is sufficient for accountability, and why the people of the interval (ahl al-fatra) are saved.

Core Idea
Accountability requires receiving the call of your own prophet.

This lesson examines a key theological question: does the message of any prophet suffice to hold a person accountable? Al-Bajuri presents two views and endorses the position that only the specific prophet sent to a person's community matters. This directly impacts the fate of those who lived in periods without a prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own words establish the issue.
Notice the key terms: دعوة, رسول, أهل الفترة.
2
Identify the two positions
The passage presents a dispute: does the da'wa of any messenger (even Adam) suffice, or must it be the messenger specifically sent to that person? Identify both sides.
3
Understand the consequence for ahl al-fatra
Al-Bajuri declares the correct view is the second. Therefore, 'ahl al-fatra' are saved even if they changed and worshipped idols. Grasp why: they never received a valid prophetic call.
This shows the importance of prophetic communication for accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف هل يُكْتَفَى بدعوة أي رسول كان ولو آدَمَ أو لا بُدَّ من دعوة الرسول الذي أُرْسِلَ إلى هذا الشخص والصحيحُ الثاني وعليه فأهلُ الفَتْرَة ناجون؛ وإن غَيَّروا وبدلوا وعبدوا الأوثانَ.
And there is disagreement: Is the call of any messenger sufficient, even Adam, or must it be the call of the messenger who was sent to that particular person? The correct is the second, and accordingly the people of the interval (fatrah) are saved, even if they changed, altered, and worshipped idols.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage presents a scholarly dispute regarding the condition for accountability. The question: does the mere existence of a prophetic call from any prophet (including Adam) suffice for a person to be accountable, or must it be the specific prophet sent to that person? Al-Bajuri states that the correct view is the second: a person is only accountable if the call of their own prophet has reached them. Consequently, the 'people of the fatrah'—those who lived in periods between prophets without any messenger—are saved (i.e., not punished for disbelief), even if they practiced idolatry and changed the original religion, because they did not receive a valid prophetic call.

Key Terms
دعوة
رسول
أهل الفترة
ناجون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any knowledge of God or any prophetic message suffices for accountability, regardless of whether the prophet was sent to that person.
Correction: Al-Bajuri clarifies that only the da'wa of the messenger sent specifically to that person is sufficient. People who never received such a message are not accountable and are saved.

Checkpoint
What is the correct view regarding the sufficiency of a prophet's da'wa according to al-Bajuri?
A) The da'wa of any prophet suffices
B) Only the da'wa of the prophet sent specifically to that person counts
C) No da'wa is needed for accountability
D) Only the da'wa of Muhammad suffices

Key Takeaway
The people of the fatrah are saved because they did not receive a valid prophetic call from a messenger specifically sent to them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you truly received the call of Prophet Muhammad ﷺ in a way that makes you accountable, or are you relying on a vague cultural Islam? What would change if you took that accountability seriously today?
?
The people of the fatrah are saved despite their idolatry because they lacked a specific call. If you have that call, what excuse do you have for any neglect? Start now: what one act of obedience will you commit today as a response to that call?
?
This passage shows that Allah's mercy considers even the technicality of not receiving a prophet. How does that challenge any self-righteousness or condemnation you hold toward others? Will you leave judgment to Allah and focus on your own response to His message?

Hadith of the Revival of the Prophet's Parents
Al-Bajuri recounts the hadith of the revival of the Prophet's parents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith about the revival of the Prophet's parents and the basis for its authenticity according to Ash'ari scholars.

Core Idea
The hadith of the parents' revival shows Allah's power to honor His Prophet with miracles.

This lesson discusses a specific hadith that some scholars accept regarding the Prophet's parents being temporarily revived to believe. Al-Bajuri presents the narration along with supporting statements from al-Suhayli and a poem, indicating that accepting such a hadith is a matter of 'realization' (haqiqah) rather than weak transmission.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith text
Read the narration from 'A'ishah and note the request for revival, the response, and the subsequent death. Consider that this is a miraculous event.
2
Examine al-Suhayli's comment
Al-Suhayli affirms that God is capable and may honor His prophet. This frames the hadith as a divine favor.
3
Consider the poetic endorsement
The poem asserts certainty about the event and dismisses those who weaken it as 'devoid of reality'. Reflect on how poetry is used in kalam discussions.
4
Note al-Suyuti's works
Al-Suyuti wrote works on the salvation of the Prophet's parents. This shows the topic's importance in later scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا الحديث هو ما روي عن عروة عن عائشة رضي الله عنهما أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سأل ربه أن يحيي له أبويه، فأحياهما له، فآمنا به، ثم أماتهما. قال السهيلي: والله قادر على كل شيء له أن يخص نبيه بما شاء من فضله، وينعم عليه بما شاء من كرامته. اهـ. ولعل هذا الحديث صح عند بعض أهل الحقيقة كما أشار إليه بعضهم بقوله: أيقنت أن أبا النبي وأمه أحياهما الرب الكريم الباري حتى له شهدا بصدق رسالة صدق فتلك كرامة المختار هذا الحديث ومن يقول بضعفه فهو الضعيف عن الحقيقة عاري
وقد ألف الجلال السيوطي مؤلفات فيما يتعلق بنجاتهما، فجزاه الله خيراً. (قوله: شرعاً) أي: بالشرع بناءً على أن جميع الأحكام ثبتت بالشرع، لكن بشرط العقل، خلافاً للماتريدية القائلين: بأن وجوب معرفة الله تعالى ثبتت بالعقل لوضوحها بخلاف سائر الأحكام والمعتزلة القائلين بأن جميع الأحكام ثبتت بالعقل والشرع إنما جاء مقوياً له.
حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري
(قوله: هذا الحديث) مبتدأ وخبر أي هذا الحديث المعول عليه الذي لا ينبغي أن يشك فيه.
(قوله: أي: بالشرع) أشار بذلك إلى أنه منصوب على نزع الخافض على القول بقياسية ذلك، والمراد بالشرع - كما في حاشية الهدهدي -: بعثة الرسل. (قوله: لوضوحها) أي: وضوح وجوبها، لا وضوح متعلقاتها التي هي العقائد تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي
(قوله: خلافاً للماتريدية القائلين: بأن وجوب المعرفة... إلخ) أي: لوضوحه، لا للتحسين كما قالت المعتزلة والمراد بعض الماتريدية؛ إذ المتقدمون منهم من علماء ما وراء النهر كالأشاعرة كما في شرح منقذة العبيد للعلامة الجوهري (1) (1) "منقذة العبيد من ربقة التقليد للشيخ أحمد بن عبد الكريم الخالدي المعروف بالجوهري المتوفى سنة (١١٨٢هـ)."
This hadith is what was narrated by 'Urwah from 'A'ishah (may Allah be pleased with them both) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) asked his Lord to revive his parents for him, so He revived them for him, and they believed in him, then He caused them to die. Al-Suhayli said: Allah is capable of everything; He may single out His prophet with whatever grace He wills and bestow upon him whatever honor He wills. End. Perhaps this hadith is authentic according to some people of realization, as some of them indicated by his saying: 'I am certain that the Prophet's father and mother were revived by the generous, Creator Lord until they testified to the truth of his message; so believe! That is the honor of the Chosen One. This hadith – and whoever says it is weak is weak, devoid of reality.' And al-Suyuti authored works regarding their salvation, may Allah reward him. (His saying: 'by divine law (shar'an)') i.e., by the divine law, based on the fact that all rulings are established by the divine law, but with the condition of reason, contrary to the Maturidis who say that the obligation to know Allah is established by reason due to its clarity, unlike other rulings, and the Mu'tazila who say that all rulings are established by reason and the divine law only came to strengthen it. Marginal note of al-Ajhuri: (His saying: 'this hadith') is a subject and predicate, i.e., this hadith is relied upon and should not be doubted. (His saying: 'i.e., by the divine law') he indicated by this that it is in the accusative case due to the removal of the preposition according to the view of its analogy, and what is meant by the divine law – as in the Hashiyah of al-Hadadi – is the sending of messengers. (His saying: 'due to its clarity') i.e., the clarity of its obligation, not the clarity of its objects which are the creeds. Taqrirat of al-Allamah Muhammad al-Anbabi: (His saying: 'contrary to the Maturidis who say that the obligation of knowledge... etc.') i.e., due to its clarity, not for improvement as the Mu'tazila said, and what is meant is some Maturidis, for the early ones among them from the scholars of Transoxiana are like the Ash'aris as in the commentary of Munqidhat al-'Ubayd by al-Allamah al-Jawhari (1) (1) 'Munqidhat al-'Ubayd min Rabqat al-Taqlid' by Shaykh Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Karim al-Khalidi known as al-Jawhari, died 1182 AH.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a historical report and a theological definition. It first presents the hadith of the Prophet's parents being revived and believing, along with al-Suhayli's comment affirming God's power and the poem supporting authenticity. It then notes al-Suyuti's works on this topic. The passage then defines the term 'shar'an' (by divine law) from the original text, explaining that all rulings are established by divine law but with the condition of reason, contrasting this Ash'ari position with the Maturidi view (obligation to know God by reason) and the Mu'tazila view (all rulings by reason, law as reinforcement). The marginal notes by al-Ajhuri grammatically explain 'هذا الحديث' and 'أي: بالشرع', clarifying that 'shar'an' means the sending of messengers. Al-Anbabi's taqrirat further explain that the Maturidis' position is based on clarity, not improvement, and that some early Maturidis from Transoxiana are like Ash'aris.

Key Terms
الحديث
إحياء
السهيلي
الحقيقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim the hadith of the revival of the Prophet's parents is definitively weak or fabricated.
Correction: Al-Bajuri shows that many reputable scholars accept it as authentic, citing al-Suhayli, a poetic endorsement, and al-Suyuti's works.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith, what did the Prophet ask his Lord to do?
A) To revive his parents for him
B) To make his parents rich
C) To forgive his parents
D) To protect his parents

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the parents' revival is considered sound by many Ash'ari scholars as a divine honor for the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah can do anything, even revive the dead as an honor to His Prophet? Or do you subconsciously limit His power based on what seems 'normal' to you? This week, examine your heart for any hidden doubt about Allah's absolute power, and ask Him to increase your certainty.
?
When you hear a report like this that challenges your previous understanding, do you dismiss it quickly or pause to consider that there may be deeper realities beyond what you know? Commit to not rejecting any possibility about Allah's actions without evidence, and ask yourself: are you humble enough to accept that your knowledge is limited?

Defining 'Shar'an' and the Role of Reason
Al-Bajuri defines 'shar'an' and contrasts with Maturidi and Mu'tazila views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari definition of 'shar'an' as the sending of messengers and how it differs from Maturidi and Mu'tazila views on reason and divine law.

Core Idea
In kalam, 'shar'an' refers to the sending of messengers, and reason's role is conditionally necessary.

This lesson clarifies a key term in kalam: 'shar'an' (by divine law). Al-Bajuri explains that all rulings are established by divine law, but with the condition of reason. He then contrasts this with the Maturidi position that the obligation to know God is known by reason alone, and the Mu'tazila position that all rulings are known by reason with revelation as reinforcement. Marginal notes further specify that 'shar'an' means the sending of messengers, not just texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of shar'an
Read the opening phrase: 'أي: بالشرع بناءً على أن جميع الأحكام ثبتت بالشرع، لكن بشرط العقل'. Understand that rulings come from divine law but reason is a condition.
2
Contrast with Maturidi view
The Maturidis hold that the obligation to know God is established by reason alone. Note that al-Bajuri says this is 'due to its clarity'.
3
Contrast with Mu'tazila view
The Mu'tazila say all rulings are established by reason, and divine law only strengthens them. This is a more radical rationalism.
4
Examine the marginal notes
Al-Ajhuri specifies that 'shar'an' means the sending of messengers (بعثة الرسل). Also note the grammatical explanation and the clarification that early Maturidis like Ash'aris.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Obligatory Knowledge of the Prophets and the Use of 'Mithl'
Al-Bajuri explains the knowledge required about prophets and why the word 'mithl' is inserted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the word 'mithl' is inserted when describing the attributes of prophets, and why only messengers are mentioned in this context.

Core Idea
Prophetic attributes resemble God's but are not identical; 'mithl' prevents confusion.

In this passage, Al-Bajuri explains the knowledge required concerning the prophets. He clarifies that a mukallaf must know 'the like of' what is obligatory, impossible, and possible for God, but applied to the messengers. The insertion of 'mithl' is crucial to avoid equating prophetic attributes with divine attributes. The passage also distinguishes between messengers and other prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of the flow, then read the English translation to understand the meaning.
Focus on the structure: there is a main statement and then marginal notes.
2
Identify the three categories
The passage refers to the three rational judgments (obligatory, impossible, possible) applied to prophets. Notice the deliberate use of 'mithl' (like) before describing them.
These categories are the same as for God, but they are not identical in reality.
3
Understand the reason for 'mithl'
The commentary explains that 'mithl' prevents the mistaken belief that prophetic attributes are identical to God's. Without 'mithl', one might imagine they are the very same.
4
Distinguish between messengers and prophets
Notice why the author mentions only messengers (rusul) and not prophets (anbiya') in general. The obligation of tabligh (delivery) applies specifically to messengers.
Non-messenger prophets are not required to deliver a new message.
5
Consider the marginal notes
The marginal notes clarify the meaning of 'iqham' (insertion) and answer a possible objection about the interpretation of 'messengers'.
The notes show the precision of the author's language.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: وَكَذَا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ :أي: ويجب عليه كذا يعني شر شرعاً. (وقوله: أنْ يَعْرِفُ مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ أي: مثل ما يجبُ في حق الله وما يستحيل وما يجوز، وإنما أَقْحَمَ لفظ (مثل) إشارةً إلى أن كلاً مما يجبُ وما يستحيل وما يجوز في حق الرسل غيرُه في حقه تعالى؛ ولو أسقطه لتوهم أنه عينه. (قوله: فِي حَقِّ الرُّسُلِ) إنما سَكَتَ عن الأنبياء غير الرسل نظراً إلى أن مجموع الأحكام الآتية - التي من جُمْلَتِها وجوبُ التبليغ واستحالة ضده - إنما يأتي في الرُّسُل دون الأنبياء غيرِ الرُّسُل، وما قيل من أنه يَجِبُ على النبي أن يُبَلِّغَ الناس نبي ليُحْتَرَمَ؛ لا يخفى أنه تَبْعُدُ إرادته هنا. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري (قوله: وَإِنَّمَا أَقْحَمَ) المراد بإقحامها: الإتيان بها، وليس المراد به: زيادة ما لا فائدة فيه كما يعلم من كلامه. (قوله: وَمَا قِيلَ... إلخ) جواب عن سؤال تقديره: يمكن حمل الرسل هنا على تقريرات العلامة محمد الألبابي .
(His statement: 'and likewise it is obligatory upon him') i.e., it is obligatory upon him something, meaning according to the Law. (And His statement: 'that he know the like of that') i.e., the like of what is obligatory concerning God and what is impossible and what is possible. And he only inserted the word 'mithl' (like) as an indication that each of what is obligatory, impossible, and possible concerning the messengers is other than it concerning Him, Exalted; and if he omitted it, one would imagine that it is the very same. (His statement: 'concerning the messengers') he only remained silent concerning the prophets other than the messengers, considering that the totality of the coming rulings—among which is the obligation of delivery (tabligh) and the impossibility of its opposite—only come concerning the messengers, not the prophets other than the messengers. And what has been said that it is obligatory upon the prophet to deliver the people to a prophet in order to be respected; it is not hidden that its intent here is far-fetched. Marginal note: (His statement: 'and he only inserted (aqhama)') the meaning of 'iqham' (insertion) is bringing it, not meaning an addition that has no benefit, as is known from his speech. (His statement: 'and what has been said... etc.') is an answer to a question whose form is: it is possible to interpret the messengers here as the determinations (taqrirat) of the scholar Muhammad al-Albabi.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage explains the knowledge required concerning the prophets. It begins by stating that just as knowledge of the three categories (obligatory, impossible, possible) is required for God, similarly a mukallaf must know 'the like of that' (mithl dhalika) regarding the messengers. The insertion of the word 'mithl' (like) is deliberate: it indicates that the attributes of the messengers are not identical to God's attributes; they are similar in kind but distinct in actuality. If 'mithl' were omitted, one might mistakenly think that the same attributes apply to both God and messengers, leading to anthropomorphism or shirk. The passage then notes that the author of the matn only mentions 'messengers' (rusul) and not 'prophets' (anbiya') in general, because the specific rulings that follow—such as the obligation of delivering the message (tabligh) and the impossibility of its opposite—apply only to messengers who are tasked with delivering a new law, not to non-messenger prophets. The marginal note clarifies that 'iqham' (insertion) simply means 'bringing' the word, not adding something useless. Another note answers a possible objection: perhaps 'messengers' here could be understood as the determinations (taqrirat) of a scholar, but that interpretation is rejected as far-fetched.

Key Terms
مثل
حق الرسل
إقحام
تبليغ
رسل
أنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the attributes of prophets (obligatory, impossible, possible) are exactly the same as God's attributes.
Correction: The word 'mithl' (like) indicates similarity but not identity. The attributes of prophets are distinct from God's attributes, though they share the same categories.

Checkpoint
Why did the author insert the word 'mithl' (like) when speaking of the attributes of the messengers?
A) To indicate that the attributes of the messengers are exactly the same as God's.
B) To indicate that the attributes of the messengers are similar but not identical to God's, preventing confusion.
C) To make the sentence grammatically correct.
D) To emphasize that the messengers are equal to God.

Key Takeaway
The insertion of 'mithl' ensures that the attributes of prophets are understood as similar but not identical to God's, preventing anthropomorphic confusion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Why do you think the scholars were so careful to insert the word 'mithl'? What does this caution reveal about the danger of confusing creation with the Creator in your own thoughts? Commit to guarding your tongue and heart from any statement that blurs the line between God and His prophets.
?
Have you ever attributed to a prophet a quality that belongs only to God, such as being all-knowing or independent? This lesson teaches that prophetic attributes are only 'like' God's. How will you actively check your beliefs about the prophets starting today?
?
The word 'mithl' prevents the mistaken notion that prophetic attributes are identical to God's. Reflect on your worship: does your love for the Prophet ever border on the kind of reverence due only to Allah? Repent of any exaggeration and realign your heart.

The Role of the Word 'Like' (مثل) in Distinguishing Attributes
Al-Bajuri explains why the word 'like' is inserted when referring to the attributes of messengers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author inserted the word 'like' when referring to the attributes of messengers and how it prevents confusing divine and prophetic attributes.

Core Idea
The word 'like' preserves the distinction between God's attributes and those of His messengers.

In this passage, Al-Bajuri explains a subtle but crucial point in Sanusi's text: the insertion of the word 'like' (مثل) when describing the attributes that messengers must possess. This word, far from being redundant, signals that the attributes of messengers are analogous to God's attributes but not identical. Without it, one might mistakenly think that messengers share the same specific attributes as God. Let us see how this careful wording protects correct theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation, paying attention to the phrase 'مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ'.
Notice how the author explains the purpose of 'مثل'.
2
Understand the need for 'like'
The author says the word 'like' was inserted to indicate that the attributes for messengers are other than those for God. Why is this important?
Without it, one would think the attributes are identical, leading to anthropomorphism or shirk.
3
Examine the marginal note on 'إقحام'
The marginal note clarifies that 'إقحام' here means 'insertion' with a purpose, not an unnecessary addition.
4
Reflect on the theological principle
Consider how this distinction protects the transcendence of God while affirming the moral excellence of prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَوْلُهُ: وَكَذَا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ :أي: ويجب عليه كذا يعني شرعاً. (وقوله: أنْ يَعْرِفُ مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ أي: مثل ما يجبُ في حق الله وما يستحيل وما يجوز، وإنما أَقْحَمَ لفظ (مثل) إشارةً إلى أن كلاً مما يجبُ وما يستحيل وما يجوز في حق الرسل غيرُه في حقه تعالى؛ ولو أسقطه لتوهم أنه عينه. (قوله: فِي حَقِّ الرُّسُلِ) إنما سَكَتَ عن الأنبياء غير الرسل نظراً إلى أن مجموع الأحكام الآتية - التي من جُمْلَتِها وجوبُ التبليغ واستحالة ضده - إنما يأتي في الرُّسُل دون الأنبياء غيرِ الرُّسُل، وما قيل من أنه يَجِبُ على النبي أن يُبَلِّغَ الناس نبي ليُحْتَرَمَ؛ لا يخفى أنه تَبْعُدُ إرادته هنا. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري (قوله: وَإِنَّمَا أَقْحَمَ) المراد بإقحامها: الإتيان بها، وليس المراد به: زيادة ما لا فائدة فيه كما يعلم من كلامه. (قوله: وَمَا قِيلَ... إلخ) جواب عن سؤال تقديره: يمكن حمل الرسل هنا على الأنبياء بأن يراد بهم من أمر بالتبليغ ويجعل التبليغ شاملاً لتبليغ النبي للناس أنه نبي ليحترم، وحاصل الجواب أن هذا المعنى تبعد إرادته هنا؛ لأن المتبادر من الرسل المأمورون بتبليغ الأحكام. (قوله: مِنْ بَابِ تَقْدِيمِ التَّخْلِيَةِ ... إلخ) فيه نوع بَشَاعَةٍ، وقال بعض مشايخنا: لا تتوهم أن المُخَلَّى المحلّى: الحقُّ، بل الخلق تتخلى نفوسهم من العقد الزائغ بعد ذكر المحبوب، ثم تتحلى بالعقد الصحيح.
And his saying: 'And likewise it is obligatory upon him' meaning: and it is obligatory upon him thus, i.e., legally. (And his saying: 'that he knows the like of that' meaning: like what is obligatory with respect to God, and what is impossible, and what is permissible. He only inserted the word 'like' as an indication that each of what is obligatory, impossible, and permissible with respect to the messengers is other than it with respect to Him, Exalted; and had he omitted it, it would be thought that it is identical. (His saying: 'with respect to the messengers') he only remained silent about the prophets other than messengers considering that the totality of the coming rulings—which include the obligation of conveying and the impossibility of its opposite—only apply to messengers, not to prophets other than messengers. And what is said that it is obligatory upon a prophet to convey to the people that he is a prophet so that he be respected—it is not hidden that its intention here is far. Commentary of the scholar Ahmad al-Ujhuri: (His saying: 'he only inserted') the intended meaning of its insertion is: bringing it, and not intending by it an increase that has no benefit, as is known from his speech. (His saying: 'and what is said... etc.') is an answer to a question whose estimation is: it is possible to interpret the messengers here as prophets, intending by them those commanded to convey, and making the conveyance inclusive of the prophet's conveying to the people that he is a prophet to be respected. The summary of the answer is that this meaning is far from intention here, because what is understood from 'messengers' is those commanded to convey rulings. (His saying: 'from the chapter of giving priority to emptying... etc.') in it there is a type of repulsiveness. And some of our teachers said: do not imagine that the one emptied and adorned is the Truth; rather, the created beings empty their souls from the deviant creed after mentioning the Beloved, then they adorn themselves with the correct creed.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory and refutational passage. Al-Bajuri explains the statement 'and likewise it is obligatory upon him' from the text, clarifying that the obligated person must know the like of what is obligatory, impossible, and permissible for God, but applied to messengers. The insertion of the word 'like' (مثل) is deliberate, signaling that the attributes for messengers are not identical to those for God; otherwise, omission would lead to confusion. The author then addresses why the text specifies 'messengers' rather than 'prophets' in general: the rulings that follow, such as the obligation of conveying (tabligh) and the impossibility of its opposite, apply specifically to messengers. An objection is raised that a prophet must convey that he is a prophet to be respected, but the response clarifies that the primary understanding of 'messengers' is those commanded to convey rulings. The marginal note from Ahmad al-Ujhuri further explains that the insertion of 'like' does not mean a superfluous addition, and the objection's answer is that the intended meaning is far-fetched. Another marginal note addresses the phrase 'giving priority to emptying before adorning,' warning against misunderstanding that the one emptied and adorned is God; rather, it is the believers who empty themselves of false beliefs and adorn themselves with correct creed.

إقحام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the attributes of prophets are exactly the same as God's attributes.
Correction: The author emphasizes that they are 'like' (مثل) the divine attributes, meaning analogous but distinct.

Checkpoint
Why does the author insert the word 'like' (مثل) when referring to the attributes of messengers?
A) To emphasize that the attributes are identical
B) To indicate that they are similar but not identical
C) To make the sentence grammatically correct
D) To show that messengers have no attributes

Key Takeaway
The word 'like' preserves the distinction between divine and prophetic attributes, preventing the error of equating them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Why Messengers Specifically? The Scope of Prophetic Obligations
Al-Bajuri explains why the text specifies 'messengers' and answers an objection about a prophet's duty to convey.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the text specifies 'messengers' (الرسل) rather than 'prophets' (الأنبياء) in the context of the obligation to know these attributes and the objection concerning a prophet's duty to convey his prophethood.

Core Idea
The obligation to convey revelation applies specifically to messengers, not all prophets.

In this section, Al-Bajuri addresses a subtle distinction: the text speaks of 'messengers' rather than 'prophets' when listing the attributes to be known. He explains that the rulings that follow, such as the obligation of conveying (tabligh) and the impossibility of its opposite, apply only to messengers. An objection is raised that a prophet must also convey his status as a prophet to be respected, but the response clarifies that the primary meaning of 'messenger' is one commanded to convey divine rulings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the distinction between 'messengers' and 'prophets'.
2
Understand the reason for specifying 'messengers'
Al-Bajuri says the author remained silent about non-messenger prophets because the coming rulings (like tabligh) only apply to messengers.
The obligation of conveying (وجوب التبليغ) is a key attribute of messengers.
3
Examine the objection and answer
Someone might argue that even a prophet must convey that he is a prophet. The response is that this interpretation is 'far' (تبعد إرادته) because the common understanding of 'messenger' is one commissioned to deliver rulings.
The objection is considered and refuted.
4
Consider the theological implications
This distinction highlights the special role of messengers in conveying divine law, as opposed to prophets who may receive inspiration but are not necessarily charged with delivering a new law.

A Caution on 'Emptying before Adorning' (تقديم التخلية على التحلية)
Al-Bajuri warns against misinterpreting 'emptying before adorning' as applying to Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle of 'giving priority to emptying before adorning' and the caution against misapplying it to Allah.

Core Idea
The process of emptying false beliefs and adorning with true creed applies to believers, not to Allah.

This brief marginal note addresses a phrase used in theological texts: 'giving priority to emptying before adorning' (تقديم التخلية على التحلية). The author warns against a potential misunderstanding: one might think that the one being emptied and adorned is Allah, but in fact it is the believer's soul that is first emptied of deviant beliefs and then adorned with correct creed. This lesson clarifies the correct application of this principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation of this short note.
2
Understand the phrase 'emptying before adorning'
This is a pedagogical principle: one must first remove false ideas before instilling correct ones.
It is often used in spiritual purification.
3
Identify the warning
The author says there is a 'type of repulsiveness' (نوع بشاعة) in the phrase if misunderstood.
The warning is not to imagine that Allah is the subject of emptying and adorning.
4
Apply the correct meaning
It is the created beings (الخلق) who empty their souls from false creed and then adorn with true creed, after mentioning the Beloved (i.e., Allah).
This preserves divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(وقوله: أنْ يَعْرِفُ مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ أي: مثل ما يجبُ في حق الله وما يستحيل وما يجوز، وإنما أَقْحَمَ لفظ (مثل) إشارةً إلى أن كلاً مما يجبُ وما يستحيل وما يجوز في حق الرسل غيرُه في حقه تعالى؛ ولو أسقطه لتوهم أنه عينه. (قوله: فِي حَقِّ الرُّسُلِ) إنما سَكَتَ عن الأنبياء غير الرسل نظراً إلى أن مجموع الأحكام الآتية - التي من جُمْلَتِها وجوبُ التبليغ واستحالة ضده - إنما يأتي في الرُّسُل دون الأنبياء غيرِ الرُّسُل، وما قيل من أنه يَجِبُ على النبي أن يُبَلِّغَ الناس نبي ليُحْتَرَمَ؛ لا يخفى أنه تَبْعُدُ إرادته هنا. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري (قوله: وَإِنَّمَا أَقْحَمَ) المراد بإقحامها: الإتيان بها، وليس المراد به: زيادة ما لا فائدة فيه كما يعلم من كلامه. (قوله: وَمَا قِيلَ... إلخ) جواب عن سؤال تقديره: يمكن حمل الرسل هنا على الأنبياء بأن يراد بهم من أمر بالتبليغ ويجعل التبليغ شاملاً لتبليغ النبي للناس أنه نبي ليحترم، وحاصل الجواب أن هذا المعنى تبعد إرادته هنا؛ لأن المتبادر من الرسل المأمورون بتبليغ الأحكام. (قوله: مِنْ بَابِ تَقْدِيمِ التَّخْلِيَةِ ... إلخ) فيه نوع بَشَاعَةٍ، وقال بعض مشايخنا: لا تتوهم أن المُخَلَّى المحلّى: الحقُّ، بل الخلق تتخلى نفوسهم من العقد الزائغ بعد ذكر المحبوب، ثم تتحلى بالعقد الصحيح.
And his saying: 'And likewise it is obligatory upon him' meaning: and it is obligatory upon him thus, i.e., legally. (And his saying: 'that he knows the like of that' meaning: like what is obligatory with respect to God, and what is impossible, and what is permissible. He only inserted the word 'like' as an indication that each of what is obligatory, impossible, and permissible with respect to the messengers is other than it with respect to Him, Exalted; and had he omitted it, it would be thought that it is identical. (His saying: 'with respect to the messengers') he only remained silent about the prophets other than messengers considering that the totality of the coming rulings—which include the obligation of conveying and the impossibility of its opposite—only apply to messengers, not to prophets other than messengers. And what is said that it is obligatory upon a prophet to convey to the people that he is a prophet so that he be respected—it is not hidden that its intention here is far. Commentary of the scholar Ahmad al-Ujhuri: (His saying: 'he only inserted') the intended meaning of its insertion is: bringing it, and not intending by it an increase that has no benefit, as is known from his speech. (His saying: 'and what is said... etc.') is an answer to a question whose estimation is: it is possible to interpret the messengers here as prophets, intending by them those commanded to convey, and making the conveyance inclusive of the prophet's conveying to the people that he is a prophet to be respected. The summary of the answer is that this meaning is far from intention here, because what is understood from 'messengers' is those commanded to convey rulings. (His saying: 'from the chapter of giving priority to emptying... etc.') in it there is a type of repulsiveness. And some of our teachers said: do not imagine that the one emptied and adorned is the Truth; rather, the created beings empty their souls from the deviant creed after mentioning the Beloved, then they adorn themselves with the correct creed.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory and refutational passage. Al-Bajuri explains the statement 'and likewise it is obligatory upon him' from the text, clarifying that the obligated person must know the like of what is obligatory, impossible, and permissible for God, but applied to messengers. The insertion of the word 'like' (مثل) is deliberate, signaling that the attributes for messengers are not identical to those for God; otherwise, omission would lead to confusion. The author then addresses why the text specifies 'messengers' rather than 'prophets' in general: the rulings that follow, such as the obligation of conveying (tabligh) and the impossibility of its opposite, apply specifically to messengers. An objection is raised that a prophet must convey that he is a prophet to be respected, but the response clarifies that the primary understanding of 'messengers' is those commanded to convey rulings. The marginal note from Ahmad al-Ujhuri further explains that the insertion of 'like' does not mean a superfluous addition, and the objection's answer is that the intended meaning is far-fetched. Another marginal note addresses the phrase 'giving priority to emptying before adorning,' warning against misunderstanding that the one emptied and adorned is God; rather, it is the believers who empty themselves of false beliefs and adorn themselves with correct creed.

Key Terms
تقديم التخلية على التحلية
بشاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the principle of 'emptying before adorning' applies to Allah (i.e., that He is the one being emptied and adorned).
Correction: It applies to the believer's soul: they empty false beliefs and adorn with true creed.

Checkpoint
What is the warning in the marginal note about 'emptying before adorning'?
A) That the phrase is grammatically incorrect
B) That one should not imagine Allah is the subject of emptying and adorning
C) That the process should be reversed
D) That only messengers can be adorned

Key Takeaway
The principle of emptying before adorning describes the believer's spiritual journey, not any change in Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself assuming that your own process of 'emptying and adorning' somehow changes Allah's nature or mercy? What does this lesson reveal about that assumption, and how will you reset your understanding today?
?
The passage warns of 'repulsiveness' in misinterpreting the phrase. Is there any area of your creed where you have unconsciously applied human processes to Allah, treating Him as if He changes or adapts? What specific step will you take to ensure your heart's purification is about you, not about redefining the Divine?
?
After mentioning the Beloved, you empty and adorn. When was the last time you truly mentioned Allah with such depth that it drove you to actively remove a false belief or habit? What will you do today to make that sequence real in your life again?

Prophethood

The Permissibility of Sending Prophets
Al-Bajuri affirms permissibility of sending prophets and refutes the Mu'tazila and Barāhima.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sunni theology holds that sending prophets is a permissible act of God, not obligatory, and how al-Bajuri refutes the Mu'tazila and Barāhima.

Core Idea
Prophethood is a gracious gift, not a divine obligation.

Al-Bajuri continues his discussion of rational judgments by addressing the sending of prophets. He affirms that it is permissible for God, contrary to two deviant groups: the Mu'tazila, who claim it is obligatory based on their principle of al-aṣlaḥ, and the Barāhima, who reject prophethood altogether. This lesson unpacks these refutations and clarifies the Sunni position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the flow. Note that it begins by stating the Sunni position and then immediately engages with opposing views.
The passage ends mid-sentence; the continuation will be covered in the next lesson.
2
Identify the two refutations
Look for how al-Bajuri refutes the Mu'tazila (who demand obligation) and the Barāhima (who reject prophethood entirely). Notice the arguments he attributes to each group.
The Mu'tazila argument is based on conflict resolution; the Barāhima rely on reason alone.
3
Reflect on the Sunni position
Consider why the Sunni view preserves God's absolute freedom and grace. Prophethood is a favor, not a debt owed by God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن الجائز في حقه تعالى: بِعْثَةُ الرُّسُل عليهم الصلاة والسلام، خلافاً للمعتزلة في قولهم بأنها واجِبَةً عليه تعالى بناءً على أصلهم الفاسد ومعتقدهم الكاسد من أنه يَجِبُ عليه تعالى فِعْلُ الصلاح والأصلاح، وقد وجهوا ذلك بأن آراء الناس تختلفُ وتتفاوت، فيقعُ التنازُعُ والتظالم، فالصلاحُ أن يُقيم لهم سفيراً مؤيَّداً بالمعجزات، فينقاد له الكل. وخلافاً للبَرَاهِمَةِ: وهم طائفةٌ كُفَّارٌ من الهند أصحاب برهام كما في شرح المقاصد، يَتْبَعُون ما حَسَّنَه العقل دون الشرع، فيستقبحون ذَبْحَ الحيوان لما فيه من التعذيب، ويستقبحون الصلاة لما فيها من وضع الوجه الذي
And among that which is permissible with respect to Him, exalted, is the sending of messengers – peace and blessings be upon them – contrary to the Muʿtazila in their statement that it is obligatory upon Him, based on their corrupt principle and degenerate belief that He must do what is beneficial and most beneficial. They justified that by [saying] that people's opinions differ and vary, so conflict and oppression occur, so the beneficial thing is for Him to establish an envoy supported by miracles, to whom everyone submits. And contrary to the Barāhima: they are a disbelieving sect from India, followers of Barham, as in Sharḥ al-Maqāṣid; they follow what reason deems good without [considering] revelation, so they deem it repugnant to slaughter animals because of the torture involved, and they deem it repugnant to pray because of placing the face which...
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
In this passage, al-Bajuri states that sending prophets is permissible (jāʾiz) for God, not obligatory. He refutes two groups: the Muʿtazila, who claim that sending prophets is obligatory based on their principle that God must do what is most beneficial (al-aṣlaḥ). The Muʿtazila argue that because people's opinions differ, conflict arises, so God must send a prophet to guide them. Al-Bajuri rejects this because God is not under obligation. Second, he refutes the Barāhima, a Hindu-influenced group who reject prophethood and follow reason alone. They find acts like animal slaughter and prayer (prostration) repugnant. Al-Bajuri notes that they follow reason without revelation, implying they are misguided. The passage ends mid-sentence on this page, likely continuing the description of their objections.

Key Terms
بعثة الرسل
الجائز
المعتزلة
البَرَاهِمَة
الصلاح
الأصلاح
برهام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God must send prophets because it is the most beneficial act, making it obligatory.
Correction: In Sunni theology, sending prophets is a voluntary act of God's grace, not an obligation; God is not bound by any external necessity.

Checkpoint
Why do the Mu'tazila claim that sending prophets is obligatory?
A) Because God promised to send prophets.
B) Because it is the most beneficial thing for humanity to resolve conflict.
C) Because the Qur'an commands it.
D) Because it is logically impossible for God not to send prophets.

Key Takeaway
Sending prophets is a permissible act of God, and the refutations of the Mu'tazila and Barāhima show that imposing obligations on God or rejecting revelation is misguided.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that God owed you no guidance, do you truly feel the weight of gratitude for the prophets He sent, or do you take them for granted? How would your relationship with your faith change if you lived each day knowing that every prophet was an undeserved mercy?
?
In what areas of your life do you still trust your own reasoning over the clear teachings of the prophets, like the Barāhima did? Are you willing to submit your intellect to revelation even when it contradicts your personal desires or logic?
?
The Mu'tazila demanded that God must act according to their notion of 'benefit.' Have you ever, even subtly, felt entitled to explanations from God about why He allowed certain hardships? How can you train your heart to accept His wisdom without imposing your own expectations on Him?

Refuting the Mu'tazila on the Obligation of Sending Messengers
Sanusi states the permissibility of sending messengers and refutes the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'aris affirm that sending messengers is permissible for God and refute the Mu'tazila's claim that it is obligatory based on the principle of al-aslah.

Core Idea
Sending messengers is possible but not obligatory on God.

In this lesson, we examine Sanusi's argument that sending messengers is among the permissible acts of God. He contrasts this with the Mu'tazila view, who erroneously claim it is obligatory based on their flawed principle that God must do what is most beneficial. Let's read the passage and see the refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice how Sanusi first states the Ash'ari position before introducing the Mu'tazila opposition.
The passage begins with 'ومن الجائز' clearly marking the permissibility.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila claim
Find the sentence where Sanusi describes the Mu'tazila belief. They say sending messengers is wajib (obligatory) on God because He must do what is good and most beneficial (wujub fi'l al-salah wa al-aslah).
Note that the Mu'tazila rely on rational necessity: they think God is compelled to do the best for creation.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila justification
Read how they justify their claim: human opinions differ, leading to conflict, so a messenger is needed to guide all. This is the 'good' they say God must provide.
This justification is based on human need, not divine nature.
4
Recognize the Ash'ari refutation
Sanusi refutes by simply stating the Mu'tazila opinion is 'corrupt' and 'rotten'. The Ash'ari position is that God is not obligated to do anything; His actions are free and not subject to rational necessity.
The refutation is concise; the longer argument is implied from earlier lessons on God's will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن الجائز في حقه تعالى: بَعْثَةُ الرُّسُل عليهم الصلاة والسلام، خلافاً للمعتزلة في قولهم بأنها واجِبَةً عليه تعالى بناءً على أصلهم الفاسد ومعتقدهم الكاسد من أنه يَجِبُ عليه تعالى فِعْلُ الصلاح والأصلاح، وقد وجهوا ذلك بأن آراء الناس تختلفُ وتتفاوت، فيقعُ التنازُعُ والتظالم، فالصلاحُ أن يُقيم لهم سفيراً مؤيَّداً بالمعجزات، فينقاد له الكل. وخلافاً للبَرَاهِمَةِ: وهم طائفةٌ كُفَّارٌ من الهند أصحاب برهام كما في شرح المقاصد، يَتْبَعُون ما حَسَّنَه العقل دون الشرع، فيستقبحون ذَبْحَ الحيوان لما فيه من التعذيب، ويستقبحون الصلاة لما فيها من وضع الوجه الذي أشرف الأعضاء على الأرض ورفع العجيزة، ويبيحون الزنا ووطة المحارم، ويقولون باستحالة بعثة الرسل. كذا نقل السنوسي عنهم. وصريح كلام السعد: أنهم يقولون : إنها جائزة، لكن لا حاجة إليها، فلا تثبت وعبارته في "شرح المقاصد": المنكرون للنبوة منهم من قال باستحالتها، ولا اعتداد به ومنهم من قال بعدم الاحتياج إليها كالبراهمة. انتهى.
And among that which is permissible with respect to Him (exalted be He) is the sending of messengers (peace and blessings be upon them), contrary to the Mu'tazila in their statement that it is obligatory upon Him (exalted be He), based on their corrupt principle and their rotten belief that He (exalted be He) must do what is good and most beneficial. They have justified this by saying that people's opinions differ and vary, leading to conflict and oppression, so it is good to appoint for them an envoy supported by miracles to whom all would submit. And contrary to the Barahima: they are a disbelieving sect from India, followers of Barham, as in Sharh al-Maqasid. They follow what reason deems good without revelation. They deem abhorrent the slaughtering of animals because of the pain it causes, and they deem abhorrent prayer because it involves placing the face, which is the noblest of limbs, on the ground and raising the buttocks, and they permit adultery and incest, and they assert the impossibility of sending messengers. Thus al-Sanusi reported from them. The explicit statement of al-Sa'd (al-Taftazani) is that they say it is permissible but there is no need for it, so it is not established. His phrase in Sharh al-Maqasid: 'The deniers of prophethood – some of them say it is impossible, and no heed is paid to them; and some of them say there is no need for it, like the Barahima.' Ended.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage discusses the attribute of sending messengers (ba'th al-rusul) as permissible (ja'iz) for God, contrary to the Mu'tazila who claim it is wajib (obligatory) based on their flawed principle that God must do what is most beneficial (al-salāh wa al-aslah). They argue that human differences necessitate a guide. The passage also refutes the Barahima, a Hindu sect that follows reason alone, rejecting revelation, and deems actions like slaughtering animals and prayer as evil, permits adultery and incest, and denies the possibility of sending messengers altogether. However, as al-Sa'd (al-Taftazani) notes in Sharh al-Maqasid, some Barahima concede the possibility but claim no need, so they reject prophethood. The Ash'ari position is that sending messengers is possible but not obligatory.

Key Terms
بعثة الرسل
الجائز
الواجب
الصلاح
الإصلاح
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Ash'aris deny God's wisdom or goodness by rejecting the principle of al-aslah.
Correction: Ash'aris affirm that God acts with wisdom but not under compulsion from reason. His actions are free, and He may choose what He wills without being obligated by human notions of 'best'.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do the Mu'tazila believe about sending messengers?
A) It is impossible for God to send messengers.
B) It is permissible but not obligatory.
C) It is obligatory upon God.
D) It is forbidden for God because it would imply need.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila error is imposing an obligation on God based on human reasoning; Ash'aris affirm that sending messengers is a free act of divine permissibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God were obligated to send you guidance, you might take it for granted. But He isn't—every prophet, every scripture is a pure gift. Does this truth make you cherish the Quran more? Or have you been treating it as something you deserve?
?
The Mu'tazila tried to impose human logic on God, saying He must do what is beneficial. Where in your life do you secretly assume God 'should' act according to your sense of fairness or benefit? Will you repent of that arrogance today?
?
Without the messengers, you would have no reliable knowledge of your Creator. Yet how often do you ignore or disobey the message they brought? If you truly believed that their coming was a free act of divine mercy, would your obedience look different starting now?

Prophethood

Refuting the Barahima on the Denial of Prophethood
Sanusi refutes the Barahima and presents their two positions on messengers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Barahima's stance on messengers—some deny their possibility, others deny their necessity—and how Sanusi refutes both views.

Core Idea
The Barahima reject messengers as either impossible or unnecessary, both false claims.

Sanusi now turns to the Barahima, a Hindu-inspired group that rejects revelation entirely. He describes their corrupt beliefs and then presents al-Taftazani's clarification that they hold two positions: some say sending messengers is impossible, others say it is possible but not needed. This lesson unpacks their arguments and the refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the Barahima
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice that Sanusi introduces the Barahima as a disbelieving sect from India, followers of Barham, who rely solely on reason.
Their name is derived from 'Barham', perhaps a founder.
2
List their corrupt beliefs
Find the egregious statements: they condemn animal slaughter and prayer, permit adultery and incest, and declare that sending messengers is impossible.
These beliefs show their rejection of divine commands.
3
Understand al-Taftazani's nuance
Read the part quoting al-Sa'd (al-Taftazani) from Sharh al-Maqasid. He reports that not all Barahima say it's impossible; some say it's possible but unnecessary.
This nuance is important: the denial of prophethood can take two forms.
4
Analyze the refutation
Sanusi refutes by labeling them as disbelievers (kuffar) and recording their immoral stances. The refutation is implicit: their absurd principles invalidate their rejection.
The quote from al-Taftazani also serves as a refutation by showing inconsistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن الجائز في حقه تعالى: بَعْثَةُ الرُّسُل عليهم الصلاة والسلام، خلافاً للمعتزلة في قولهم بأنها واجِبَةً عليه تعالى بناءً على أصلهم الفاسد ومعتقدهم الكاسد من أنه يَجِبُ عليه تعالى فِعْلُ الصلاح والأصلاح، وقد وجهوا ذلك بأن آراء الناس تختلفُ وتتفاوت، فيقعُ التنازُعُ والتظالم، فالصلاحُ أن يُقيم لهم سفيراً مؤيَّداً بالمعجزات، فينقاد له الكل. وخلافاً للبَرَاهِمَةِ: وهم طائفةٌ كُفَّارٌ من الهند أصحاب برهام كما في شرح المقاصد، يَتْبَعُون ما حَسَّنَه العقل دون الشرع، فيستقبحون ذَبْحَ الحيوان لما فيه من التعذيب، ويستقبحون الصلاة لما فيها من وضع الوجه الذي أشرف الأعضاء على الأرض ورفع العجيزة، ويبيحون الزنا ووطة المحارم، ويقولون باستحالة بعثة الرسل. كذا نقل السنوسي عنهم. وصريح كلام السعد: أنهم يقولون : إنها جائزة، لكن لا حاجة إليها، فلا تثبت وعبارته في "شرح المقاصد": المنكرون للنبوة منهم من قال باستحالتها، ولا اعتداد به ومنهم من قال بعدم الاحتياج إليها كالبراهمة. انتهى.
And among that which is permissible with respect to Him (exalted be He) is the sending of messengers (peace and blessings be upon them), contrary to the Mu'tazila in their statement that it is obligatory upon Him (exalted be He), based on their corrupt principle and their rotten belief that He (exalted be He) must do what is good and most beneficial. They have justified this by saying that people's opinions differ and vary, leading to conflict and oppression, so it is good to appoint for them an envoy supported by miracles to whom all would submit. And contrary to the Barahima: they are a disbelieving sect from India, followers of Barham, as in Sharh al-Maqasid. They follow what reason deems good without revelation. They deem abhorrent the slaughtering of animals because of the pain it causes, and they deem abhorrent prayer because it involves placing the face, which is the noblest of limbs, on the ground and raising the buttocks, and they permit adultery and incest, and they assert the impossibility of sending messengers. Thus al-Sanusi reported from them. The explicit statement of al-Sa'd (al-Taftazani) is that they say it is permissible but there is no need for it, so it is not established. His phrase in Sharh al-Maqasid: 'The deniers of prophethood – some of them say it is impossible, and no heed is paid to them; and some of them say there is no need for it, like the Barahima.' Ended.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage discusses the attribute of sending messengers (ba'th al-rusul) as permissible (ja'iz) for God, contrary to the Mu'tazila who claim it is wajib (obligatory) based on their flawed principle that God must do what is most beneficial (al-salāh wa al-aslah). They argue that human differences necessitate a guide. The passage also refutes the Barahima, a Hindu sect that follows reason alone, rejecting revelation, and deems actions like slaughtering animals and prayer as evil, permits adultery and incest, and denies the possibility of sending messengers altogether. However, as al-Sa'd (al-Taftazani) notes in Sharh al-Maqasid, some Barahima concede the possibility but claim no need, so they reject prophethood. The Ash'ari position is that sending messengers is possible but not obligatory.

Key Terms
البراهمة
برهام
شرح المقاصد
السعد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Barahima are purely rational philosophers without immoral doctrines.
Correction: Sanusi records that they permit adultery and incest, showing their rationalism leads to moral corruption.

Checkpoint
According to al-Taftazani, what do the Barahima say about the possibility of sending messengers?
A) They unanimously deem it impossible.
B) Some say it is impossible, others say it is possible but unnecessary.
C) They all say it is possible but unnecessary.
D) They believe it is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The Barahima rejection of messengers rests on either impossibility or dispensability; their self-contradictory moral stances discredit their rationalism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself trusting your own intellect over explicit commands from revelation? In what specific area of your life does that temptation arise, and what would it cost you to submit fully to God's word instead?
?
The Barahima found the prostration posture abhorrent. Have you ever felt embarrassed or reluctant about a prescribed act of worship because of what others might think? How does this lesson challenge you to abandon that hesitation?

Refraining from Specifying the Numbers of Prophets and Messengers
Al-Bajuri discusses the varying narrations and gives the ruling to refrain from specifying numbers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Bajuri advises refraining from specifying the exact numbers of prophets and messengers and instead believing in them in general.

Core Idea
Specifying numbers of prophets risks error; we believe in them in general.

Al-Bajuri begins by explaining the varying narrations about the counts of prophets and messengers. He then quotes a Quranic verse indicating that not all prophets are mentioned. From this, he concludes that the correct position is to refrain from fixing a number and to believe in them in general.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about narrations and the Quranic verse
Read the Arabic passage from the beginning up to 'على الإجمال'. Notice the differing numbers and the verse from Surah Ghafir.
The verse supports the idea that many prophets are not mentioned.
2
Identify the two problems with specifying numbers
Al-Bajuri states that specifying could wrongly affirm prophethood for a non-prophet or deny it for a true prophet. Understand why this is dangerous.
3
Understand the obligation to believe in general (ijmal)
The conclusion is that we must believe in all prophets and messengers without needing to know the exact count. Reflect on how this balances certainty and uncertainty.
This principle protects against both false claims and denial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: وَأَمَّا الرُّسُلُ... إلخ مقابل لمحذوف، والتقدير: أما الباري تقدم ما يجب في حقه وما يستحيل وما يجوز، وأما الرسل... إلخ، وإنما عَبَّر بالرسل، ولم يعتز بالأنبياء ـ مع أنه أشمل من الرُّسُل؛ لشموله لمن لم يُؤْمَرُ بالتبليغ من الأنبياء ؛ لأن مما سيذكره التبليغ وضده وهما خاصان بالرسل، أو جرياً على القول بالترادف.
وقد اختلفت الروايات في عدد كلّ من الرسل والأنبياء فروي أن الرسل ثلاثمائة وثلاثة عَشَرَ، وفي رواية وأربعةَ عَشَرَ، وفي رواية: وخمسة عشر. وروي: أن الأنبياء مائة ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفاً، وفي رواية وخمسة وعشرون ألفاً، وروي أنهم ألفُ ألف ومائتا ألف وفي رواية وأربعمائة ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفاً. الصحيحُ فيهما: الإمساك عن حضرهم في عددٍ؛ لأنه ربما أدى إلى إثبات الرسالة أو النبوة لمن ليس كذلك في الواقع، أو إلى نفي ذلك عمن هو كذلك في الواقع، وقد قال تعالى: (مِنْهُم مَّن قَصَصْنَا عَلَيْكَ وَمِنْهُم مَن لَّمْ نَقْصُصْ عَلَيْكَ) ، فيجب التصديق بأن الله رُسُلاً وأنبياء على الإجمال إلا خمسة وعشرين، فيجب معرفتهم على التفصيل كما أشار لذلك بعضهم بقوله: حَتْمٌ عَلَى كُلِّ ذِي التَّكْلِيفِ مَعْرِفَةٌ بِأَنْبِيَاءَ عَلَى التَّفْصِيلِ قَدْ عُلِمُوا فِي تِلْكَ حُجَّتُنَا مِنْهُمْ ثَمَانِيَةً مِنْ بَعْدِ عَشْرٍ، وَيَبْقَى سَبْعَةٌ وَهُمُو إدْرِيسُ هُودٌ شُعَيْبٌ صَالِحٌ وَكَذَا ذُو الْكِفْلِ آدَمُ بِالْمُخْتَارِ قَدْ خُتِمُوا. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري.
(قوله: الْقَوْل بالتَّرَادُفِ :أي: ترادف النبي والرسول على معنى واحد، وهو معنى الرسول كما في الشنشوري.
(قوله: بالْمُخْتَارِ قَدْ خُتِمُوا أي: ختموا ذكراً وخارجاً به.
His statement: 'And as for the messengers... etc.' is the counterpart of an omitted part, and the estimation is: As for the Creator, what is obligatory for Him, what is impossible, and what is contingent have preceded; and as for the messengers... etc. And he only expressed 'messengers' and not 'prophets'—although it is more comprehensive than messengers because it includes those who were not commanded to convey from among the prophets—because among what he will mention is conveying and its opposite, and these two are specific to messengers, or following the view of synonymy. And the narrations have differed regarding the number of each of the messengers and prophets. It is narrated that the messengers are three hundred and thirteen, in one narration fourteen, in another narration fifteen. And it is narrated that the prophets are one hundred thousand and twenty-four thousand, in one narration and twenty-five thousand, and it is narrated that they are one million two hundred thousand, in one narration four hundred thousand and twenty-four thousand. The correct position regarding both of them is to refrain from specifying their number; because it might lead to affirming messengerhood or prophethood for one who is not so in reality, or to denying it for one who is so in reality. And Allah said: 'Among them are those We have narrated to you and among them are those We have not narrated to you' (Quran 40:78). So it is obligatory to believe that there are messengers and prophets from Allah in general, except for twenty-five, for which it is obligatory to know them in detail, as some pointed out by his saying: 'It is an obligation upon every legally responsible person to have knowledge of prophets in detail. Those known among them are eight after ten, and seven remain: Idris, Hud, Shu'ayb, Salih, and likewise Dhul-Kifl, Adam, and the Chosen One (Muhammad) with whom they are sealed.' Marginal note by the scholar Ahmad al-Ujhuri. His statement: 'the view of synonymy' means the synonymy of prophet and messenger in one meaning, which is the meaning of messenger, as in al-Shanshuri. His statement: 'with the Chosen One they are sealed' means they are sealed in mention and in existence by him.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on Sanusi's section about the messengers. Al-Bajuri begins by explaining that the phrase 'wa amma al-rusul' (and as for the messengers) is the counterpart of an omitted part in the text; the full structure would be: 'As for the Creator, what is obligatory, impossible, and contingent for Him have been mentioned, and as for the messengers...' He then notes that Sanusi specifically said 'messengers' (rusul) rather than 'prophets' (anbiya'), even though 'prophets' is more comprehensive, because the coming discussion includes conveying revelation (tabligh) and its opposite, which are specific to messengers. Alternatively, it could be following the view that the terms are synonymous. Next, Al-Bajuri discusses the various narrations about the numbers of prophets and messengers: messengers are said to be 313, 314, or 315; prophets are said to be 124,000, 125,000, or 1,200,000 (with variations). He states that the correct position is to refrain from specifying a number, because specifying might wrongly affirm prophethood for someone who is not a prophet or deny it from someone who is. He cites Quran 40:78, which indicates there are prophets not mentioned. Therefore, it is obligatory to believe in prophets and messengers in general (ijmal), except for twenty-five whom we must know in detail (tafsil). He then quotes a poetic summary by some scholar listing the twenty-five: eight after ten (i.e., after Noah? Actually 'eight from after ten' might refer to a specific count; the poem lists Idris, Hud, Shu'ayb, Salih, Dhul-Kifl, Adam, and the Chosen One (Muhammad) as the remaining seven, but the translation clarifies). Finally, Al-Bajuri provides two marginal clarifications: first, that 'the view of synonymy' means that 'prophet' and 'messenger' are synonymous, as per al-Shanshuri; second, that 'with the Chosen One they are sealed' means they are sealed both in mention and in existence by Muhammad.

Key Terms
رسل
أنبياء
إجمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The exact number of prophets must be known.
Correction: The correct stance is to refrain from specifying because it could lead to error, as Allah says some are not narrated.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct stance regarding the exact number of prophets and messengers?
A) It is obligatory to know the exact number
B) One should refrain from specifying a number
C) The number is exactly 124,000 prophets
D) Only the messengers are to be counted

Key Takeaway
We believe in all prophets and messengers of Allah in general, without needing to know the exact count, due to the risk of error and the Quranic indication that many are not mentioned.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson teaches that specifying the exact number of prophets risks error. In your own life, where are you tempted to demand detailed knowledge from Allah that He has not given—perhaps about the unseen or future? Are you at peace with not knowing every detail, or does your heart seek certainty where Allah has placed ambiguity? Resolve to entrust one such unknown to Allah today.
?
When a trusted source gives you differing numbers or information about religious matters, do you feel unsettled? This lesson shows the prophetic practice: refrain from committing when certainty is absent. Is there a belief you hold dogmatically that might actually be uncertain? Prepare to say, 'Allah knows best' and let go of that insistence.
?
The Quran says many prophets were not narrated to us. Does this humble you? You believe in all of them without knowing their names. Are you equally content to believe in what Allah has decreed without needing to know the details of His wisdom in your own trials? Choose one area of your life where you will stop insisting on understanding and simply trust Allah's hidden plan.

The Obligation to Know the Twenty-Five Prophets in Detail
Al-Bajuri states the obligation to know twenty-five prophets in detail and provides a poetic list.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which prophets we must know in detail, their names as listed in the poetic summary, and the clarifications about synonymy and the seal.

Core Idea
Twenty-five prophets must be known in detail; the rest are believed in general.

After establishing that we believe in prophets in general, Al-Bajuri states an exception: twenty-five prophets must be known specifically. He cites a poetic summary that lists them and adds clarifications about the synonymy of 'prophet' and 'messenger' and that Muhammad (s) is the seal.

Guided Path
1
Read the exception and poetic summary
Read the Arabic from 'إلا خمسة وعشرين' to the end. Note that the poem is a mnemonic for the twenty-five prophets.
The poem is attributed to a scholar and is meant to aid memorization.
2
Identify the twenty-five prophets from the poem
The poem says 'eight after ten' and 'seven remain' and lists names: Idris, Hud, Shu'ayb, Salih, Dhul-Kifl, Adam, and Muhammad. Try to see how these might add up to twenty-five.
The exact enumeration might require external knowledge, but the passage emphasizes that twenty-five must be known.
3
Understand the clarifications on synonymy and sealing
Al-Bajuri clarifies that 'prophet' and 'messenger' can be synonymous, and that Muhammad is the seal of the prophets.
These clarifications are in the marginal notes.
