Three Categories of Prophetic Communication
Al-Bajuri explains the three categories of prophetic communication commands.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of prophetic communication regarding what prophets are commanded to do with divine information: convey, conceal, or choice.

Core Idea
Prophets are commanded to convey some things, conceal others, and given choice in between.

Al-Bajuri unpacks Sanusi's statement about prophets conveying what they are commanded, clarifying that this excludes two other categories: what they must conceal and what they have discretion over. This threefold division is essential for understanding the scope of prophetic responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Pay attention to the key terms and how they relate to the three categories.
2
Identify the three categories
From the passage, list the three categories of prophetic communication as described by Al-Bajuri. Notice how each category has a different obligation.
3
Understand the nuance about concealment
Note that the obligation to conceal is included in the concept of trust (amānah). Consider why the author mentions this connection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: وَتَبْلِيغُ مَا أُمِرُوا بِتَبْلِيغِهِ لِلْخَلْقِ احترز بقوله: (ما أمروا... إلخ) عما أمروا بكتمانه عن الخلق، وعما خُيّروا فيه، فليس تبليغ كلّ منهما واجباً، بل يجب كِتْمَانُ ما أُمِرُوا بكتمانه، ولا يجب عليهم شيءٌ فيما خُيّروا فيه، فالأقسام ثلاثة: ما أمروا بتبليغه، وما أمروا بكتمانه وما خُيروا فيه. وإنما لم يَذْكُرِ المصنف وجوبَ كتمان ما أمروا بكتمانه؛ لأنه داخل في الأمانة كما قاله في "الأسرار الإلهية".
His statement: 'and conveying what they are commanded to convey to the creation' – he restricts by his statement ('what they are commanded... etc.) excluding what they are commanded to conceal from the creation, and what they are given choice regarding. So conveying each of these two is not obligatory; rather, concealing what they are commanded to conceal is obligatory, and nothing is obligatory upon them regarding what they are given choice in. So the divisions are three: what they are commanded to convey, what they are commanded to conceal, and what they are given choice in. The author did not mention the obligation of concealing what they are commanded to conceal because it is included in the trust (amānah) as he said in 'al-Asrār al-Ilāhiyyah'.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exegesis of a line from Sanusi's text that says prophets are commanded to convey what they are ordered to convey. Al-Bajuri explains that this phrase is meant to exclude two other categories: what prophets are commanded to conceal, and what they are given choice about. For the first excluded category (what they are commanded to conceal), it is obligatory to conceal it, not to convey it. For the second excluded category (what they are given choice in), nothing is obligatory upon them at all. Thus, the overall classification of prophetic commands regarding information is threefold: mandatory conveyance, mandatory concealment, and discretionary. Al-Bajuri notes that Sanusi did not explicitly state the obligation of concealment in this context because it is already implied in the concept of trust (amānah), referencing his own work 'al-Asrār al-Ilāhiyyah'.

Key Terms
تبليغ
كتمان
تخيير
أمانة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets must convey all knowledge they receive to the people.
Correction: Prophets are commanded to conceal some things and have discretion over others, as clarified by the threefold division.

Checkpoint
How many categories of prophetic communication are mentioned in this passage?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Prophetic communication is divided into three categories: obligatory conveyance, obligatory concealment, and discretionary, reflecting the completeness of prophetic trust.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat the knowledge of Islam as a trust (amānah), carefully discerning what must be conveyed, what must be concealed, and what is left to your discretion? Or do you speak carelessly?
?
When you are commanded to convey a truth, do you do so without hesitation, or do you sometimes conceal it out of fear or convenience? How does this lesson expose your own failings?
?
If the Prophet ﷺ was given choice in some matters, are you faithful in exercising your choices only for what pleases Allah? Will you repent for the times you chose your own desire over His command?

Impossibility of Prophetic Opposites and Definition of Lying
Al-Bajuri expounds on the impossibility of prophetic opposites, defines lying, and asserts prophetic sinlessness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the opposites of prophetic attributes are impossible, how 'opposite' and 'lying' are defined in this context, and that prophets are sinless before and after prophethood, even forgetfully.

Core Idea
Prophetic attributes cannot have real opposites because what Allah makes obligatory cannot be contradicted.

This passage from al-Bajuri delves into the foundational principle that prophets are protected from any attribute contrary to their essential qualities. He clarifies technical terms like 'impossibility' and 'opposite', and defines lying as non-correspondence to reality. The commentary also addresses a common doubt about sins occurring forgetfully or before prophethood, asserting that such acts must be interpreted to preserve prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to grasp the overall argument, then read the literal translation to ensure understanding.
Notice the concise style of al-Bajuri's commentary.
2
Analyze the definitions
Focus on how al-Bajuri defines 'impossibility' and 'opposite'. What does he mean by 'impossibility by legal proof'? How does he explain 'opposite' as absolute contradictory?
These definitions are crucial for the logic of kalam.
3
Understand the definition of lying
Lying is defined as non-correspondence of a report to reality. Connect this to the definition of truthfulness and see how it applies to prophets.
4
Examine the ruling on sins
Note the assertion that minor and major sins, even forgetful ones and those before prophethood, are impossible for prophets. Consider the objection and response given by al-Bajuri.
This part preempts a common doubt about prophetic infallibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: وَيَسْتَحِيلُ فِي حَقِّهِمْ... إلخ) المراد بالاستحالة: عدم إمكان الاتصاف ولو بالدليل الشرعي؛ لأن ما وَجَبَ بدليل شرعي يستحيل ضده بدليل شرعي، وما جب بغيره يستحيل ضده بغيره كما تقدم تفصيله. (قوله: أَضْدَادُ هَذِهِ الصَّفَاتِ المراد بالضدّ هنا: مُطلَقُ المنافي؛ لأنها ليست كلَّها أضداداً كما تقدم نظيره. فيما مرّ. (قوله: الْكَذِبُ) أي: عدم مطابَقَةِ الخبر للواقع؛ لما عُلِمَ من تعريف الصدق (قوله: بِفِعْلِ شَيْءٍ... إلخ) المراد بالفعل: ما يشمل القول. واعلم أنه لا فَرْقَ بين الصغيرة والكبيرة، فلا تَقَعُ منهم صغيرة ولا كبيرة ولو سهواً، قبل البعثة وبعدها. لا يقال: ما كان سَهْواً أو قبل البعثة ليس بمعصية؛ لأنا نقول: هو صورة معصية، وما وَرَدَ مما يوهِمُ وقوع ذلك منهم يجب تأويله.
His statement: 'And it is impossible in their case... etc.' – by impossibility is meant the non-possibility of being described [with that attribute] even by a legal proof; because what is necessitated by a legal proof, its opposite is impossible by a legal proof, and what is necessitated by other than it, its opposite is impossible by other than it, as its detail preceded. His statement: 'The opposites of these attributes' – by opposite here is meant absolute contradictory (al-munāfī); because they are not all real opposites as its parallel preceded earlier. His statement: 'Lying (al-kadhib)' – i.e., non-correspondence of the report to reality; as is known from the definition of truthfulness. His statement: 'By doing something... etc.' – by action is intended what includes speech. And know that there is no difference between minor and major [sins]; so neither minor nor major occurs from them, even forgetfully, before the mission and after it. It cannot be said: what is forgetful or before the mission is not a sin; because we say: it is the form of a sin, and what has been reported that gives the impression of that occurring from them must be interpreted.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on Sanusi's statement that the opposites of prophetic attributes are impossible. Al-Bajuri defines 'impossibility' here as the real impossibility of being described with such attributes, even if a legal proof might seem to indicate otherwise. The rationale is that whatever is proven obligatory by a legal proof has its opposite impossible by that same legal proof. Similarly, attributes proven by other means have their opposites impossible by those means. The term 'opposite' is explained as absolute contradiction, not necessarily a real ontological opposite, since some alleged opposites (like lying) are privations. Lying is defined as the non-correspondence of a statement to reality, and 'action' includes speech. Al-Bajuri emphasizes that there is no difference between minor and major sins; prophets are protected from both, even forgetfully, and both before and after their prophethood. He preemptively addresses an objection: that forgetfulness or pre-prophethood actions might not be sins. He responds that such actions are still 'in the form of sin' and must be interpreted away when reported.

Key Terms
استحالة
ضد
كذب
معصية
سهو
قبل البعثة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Forgetful actions or actions before prophethood are not sins, so they could occur from prophets without compromising their perfection.
Correction: Al-Bajuri states that even forgetful or pre-prophethood actions are in the form of sin and must be interpreted away; prophets are sinless in all states.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the definition of 'lying' (al-kadhib)?
A) Intentionally stating a falsehood
B) Non-correspondence of a report to reality
C) Speaking without knowledge
D) Contradicting a previous statement

Key Takeaway
Prophets are protected from all opposites of their attributes, including lying and all sins, regardless of forgetfulness or timing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make a mistake or sin, even unintentionally or out of forgetfulness, do you excuse yourself as easily as many do regarding prophets? How does the absolute sinlessness of prophets challenge your own standard of accountability before Allah?
?
This lesson teaches that reports seeming to indicate prophetic sin must be reinterpreted. Are you willing to surrender your own preconceived interpretations of such reports, even if they are widely held? What personal attachment might you have to a mistaken narrative about a prophet?
?
Al-Bajuri says there is no distinction between minor and major sins for prophets. In your daily life, which small transgressions do you treat lightly? If a prophet would not even commit that 'minor' sin, what does that demand from you today?

Lying as a Privation of Correspondence
Al-Ajhuri defines lying as a privation and denies it is a true opposite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why lying is considered a privation (ʿadamī) and thus not a real opposite of truthfulness in kalam theology.

Core Idea
Lying is an absence, not a presence—so it cannot be a real opposite.

In the study of prophetic attributes, theologians classify opposites to define what is impossible for prophets. Lying seems to oppose truthfulness, but is it a true opposite? Al-Ajhūrī’s marginal note explains that lying is a privation (ʿadamī), meaning it lacks a positive nature, and therefore cannot be a genuine opposite.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on lying as privation
Read the Arabic sentence carefully, noting the definition of lying as non-correspondence.
This is a definition, not a proof.
2
Identify the argument
Recognize that lying is defined as an absence (ʿadam), which makes it a privative attribute, not a positive one. Hence it is not a real opposite.
Opposites require two positive existents.
3
Reflect on the theological motive
Consider why this distinction matters: if lying were a real opposite, it would be a positive attribute, potentially attributing something to the prophet. Instead, it is a mere absence, preserving infallibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري (قوله: لأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ كُلَّهَا أَضْدَاداً لأن منها الكذب، وهو عدم مطابقة الخير للواقع، فيكون أمراً عدمياً، فلا يكون ضداً حقيقة. (قوله: وَمَا وَرَدَ... إلخ) كقوله في قصة ذي اليدين لما قال له: أقصرت الصلاة أم نسيت يا رسول الله؟ كل ذلك لم يكن) فإن هذا يوهم الكذب في الظاهر، فإن بعض الأمرين وهو النسيان قد كان فيؤول ذلك على معنى كل ذلك لم يكن في ظني، وهذا صدق.
Marginal note of the scholar Aḥmad al-Ajhūrī: (His statement: 'because they are not all opposites' because among them is lying, which is the non-correspondence of the report to reality, so it is a privative matter, thus it is not a real opposite. (His statement: 'and what has been reported... etc.') like his statement in the story of Dhu al-Yadayn when he said to him: 'Has the prayer been shortened or did you forget, O Messenger of Allah? All of that was not' – for this apparently suggests lying, since one of the two matters, forgetfulness, did occur. So it is interpreted as meaning 'All of that was not in my estimation', and this is truthful.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a marginal note by al-Ajhūrī commenting on the previous discussion about opposites of prophetic attributes. He explains why not all opposites are real opposites: lying is a privation (ʿadamī), i.e., the absence of correspondence between a statement and reality, and thus not a positive entity that can be a real opposite. He then addresses a specific report that might seem to imply the Prophet uttered something untrue. The story of Dhu al-Yadayn is referenced: after the Prophet made a mistake in prayer, a companion asked if the prayer was shortened or if he forgot. The Prophet replied 'كل ذلك لم يكن' (all of that did not happen). Apparently, forgetfulness did happen, so it seems the Prophet denied something true. Al-Ajhūrī interprets this by explaining that the Prophet meant 'all of that was not in my estimation (fī ẓannī)', meaning he did not believe the prayer was shortened nor that he had forgotten in his awareness. Thus, the statement is truthful, preserving prophetic infallibility.

Key Terms
عدم
ضد
كذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think lying is a real opposite of truthfulness, like knowledge and ignorance.
Correction: Al-Ajhūrī explains that lying is a privation (absence), not a positive opposite, because it is defined as non-correspondence, not a positive attribute.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ajhūrī, why is lying not a real opposite?
A) Because it is a positive attribute
B) Because it is a privation (ʿadamī)
C) Because it does not involve speech
D) Because prophets never lie

Key Takeaway
Lying is a privation (ʿadam), not a positive opposite, because it is defined as the absence of correspondence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that lying is not a positive opposite but a mere absence of correspondence. Reflect on a lie you have told: did you experience it as the absence of truth, or did it feel like a real act? How does this shift your responsibility to actively fill your speech with truth?
?
If lying is only a privation, then every truthful statement is a presence of correspondence. How many of your daily statements are deliberately truthful? Are you comfortable with the silence where truth is absent?
?
Al-Ajhuri distinguishes between what seems to be an opposite and what truly is. What other 'opposites' in your life might actually be privations—absences of virtue rather than positive vices? What would it mean for you to treat them that way?

Interpreting the Hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn
Al-Ajhuri interprets a hadith to resolve an apparent contradiction with prophetic infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ajhūrī interprets the apparent contradiction in the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn to preserve prophetic infallibility.

Core Idea
The Prophet's words are truthful when understood as 'not in my estimation'.

A hadith relates that the Prophet, after a mistake in prayer, said 'All of that was not.' Since forgetfulness did occur, this seems to be a false statement. How do scholars reconcile this with prophetic infallibility? Al-Ajhūrī explains that the intended meaning is that the Prophet did not believe it happened, making the statement truthful.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its apparent problem
Read the passage describing the story of Dhu al-Yadayn and the Prophet's response. Note the apparent contradiction: forgetfulness occurred but the Prophet denied it.
This is a common objection against infallibility.
2
Study Al-Ajhūrī's interpretation
Al-Ajhūrī explains that the phrase 'كل ذلك لم يكن' is interpreted as 'all of that was not in my estimation' (fī ẓannī). This makes it truthful because the Prophet was unaware.
Interpretation (taʾwīl) is necessary to avoid impugning the Prophet.
3
Reflect on the principle of infallibility
Consider why such interpretations are needed: to maintain that prophets are protected from sin, including lying. The interpretation harmonizes the apparent meaning with established doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري (قوله: لأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ كُلَّهَا أَضْدَاداً لأن منها الكذب، وهو عدم مطابقة الخير للواقع، فيكون أمراً عدمياً، فلا يكون ضداً حقيقة. (قوله: وَمَا وَرَدَ... إلخ) كقوله في قصة ذي اليدين لما قال له: أقصرت الصلاة أم نسيت يا رسول الله؟ كل ذلك لم يكن) فإن هذا يوهم الكذب في الظاهر، فإن بعض الأمرين وهو النسيان قد كان فيؤول ذلك على معنى كل ذلك لم يكن في ظني، وهذا صدق.
Marginal note of the scholar Aḥmad al-Ajhūrī: (His statement: 'because they are not all opposites' because among them is lying, which is the non-correspondence of the report to reality, so it is a privative matter, thus it is not a real opposite. (His statement: 'and what has been reported... etc.') like his statement in the story of Dhu al-Yadayn when he said to him: 'Has the prayer been shortened or did you forget, O Messenger of Allah? All of that was not' – for this apparently suggests lying, since one of the two matters, forgetfulness, did occur. So it is interpreted as meaning 'All of that was not in my estimation', and this is truthful.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a marginal note by al-Ajhūrī commenting on the previous discussion about opposites of prophetic attributes. He explains why not all opposites are real opposites: lying is a privation (ʿadamī), i.e., the absence of correspondence between a statement and reality, and thus not a positive entity that can be a real opposite. He then addresses a specific report that might seem to imply the Prophet uttered something untrue. The story of Dhu al-Yadayn is referenced: after the Prophet made a mistake in prayer, a companion asked if the prayer was shortened or if he forgot. The Prophet replied 'كل ذلك لم يكن' (all of that did not happen). Apparently, forgetfulness did happen, so it seems the Prophet denied something true. Al-Ajhūrī interprets this by explaining that the Prophet meant 'all of that was not in my estimation (fī ẓannī)', meaning he did not believe the prayer was shortened nor that he had forgotten in his awareness. ?

?
The Prophet's words were truthful because they reflected his estimation at the time. Are your own words always a true reflection of what you know, or do you sometimes speak carelessly? Will you commit to being more mindful of your speech today?
?
Someone had to point out the Prophet's forgetfulness before he became aware of it. Who in your life has the courage to correct you? And are you humble enough to accept correction when you are unaware of your own faults?

Prophetic Actions Are Only Obligatory or Recommended
Al-Bajuri classifies all actions of prophets as either obligatory or recommended.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why all actions of prophets are either obligatory or recommended, and how apparent exceptions are explained.

Core Idea
Prophetic actions are never neutral—every act is either obligatory or recommended.

Al-Bajuri explains that prophets are protected from even the slightest disliked action. He addresses apparent counterexamples from the Prophet's own practice, showing that what seems permissible or disliked is actually done for a higher purpose. This lesson clarifies the unique legislative role of prophetic actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how al-Bajuri uses a compact style.
2
Understand key terms
Focus on terms like karāhah (disliked), khilāf al-ūlā (contrary to the better), tashrīʿ (legislation), and qurbah (closeness). These are central to the argument.
Khilāf al-ūlā is a category of disliked that is not sinful.
3
Identify the objection and its refutation
The objection is that the Prophet did things like urinating standing or wudu once/twice, which seem permissible or even disliked. Al-Bajuri refutes by saying these were for legislation and demonstrating permissibility.
This refutation shows that such actions are obligatory for the Prophet.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The conclusion is that all prophetic actions are either wājib (obligatory) or mandūb (recommended). They are never truly permissible, disliked, or forbidden.
This is because prophets are the elite of creation, immune from base acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: أَوْ كَرَاهَةِ المراد بها ما يشمل خِلَافَ الأولى. ولا يَردُ على ذلك: أنه بال قائماً)، وتوضأ مرَّةً مرَّةً)، وتوضأ مرَّتين مرَّتين؛ لأنه للتشريع ولبيان الجواز، وذلك واجب في حقه الله فعلِم مما تقرر أنه لا يَقَعُ منهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام محرَّم ولا مكروه على وجه كونه مكروهاً، وكذا لا يقع منهم مُبَاحٌ على وجه كونه مباحاً، بل على وجه كونه قُرْبَةً، أو للتشريع، أو للتقوي على العبادات، أو نحو ذلك، فأفعالهم دائرة بين الواجب والمندوب فقط، كيف وقد يتَّفِقُ ذلك لبعض أوليائه، فبالأولى أن يكون لصفوة الله من خلقه.
His statement: 'or disliked (karāhah)' – by it is intended what includes contrary to the better (khilāf al-ūlā). And it is not objected against that by saying: 'he urinated standing', 'he performed wudu once', 'he performed wudu twice' – because that is for legislation (tashrīʿ) and for demonstrating permissibility, and that is obligatory in his right. So know from what is established that there does not occur from them, peace and blessings be upon them, anything forbidden or disliked as being disliked, and likewise no permissible action occurs from them as being permissible, but rather as an act of closeness (qurbah), or for legislation, or for strengthening for acts of worship, or the like. So their actions revolve between the obligatory and the recommended only. How can it be otherwise, when that occurs even for some of His saints, so it is more fitting for the elite of Allah from His creation.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on Sanusi's statement that prophets are protected from disliked acts. Al-Bajuri clarifies that 'disliked' here includes even what is contrary to the better (khilāf al-ūlā). He then addresses a potential objection based on reported actions of the Prophet that might appear to be permissible or even disliked, such as urinating standing, or performing wudu once or twice. Al-Bajuri explains that such actions were done for the purpose of legislation (tashrīʿ) or to demonstrate permissibility, and thus they are actually obligatory for the Prophet as part of his mission. Consequently, prophets never perform forbidden, disliked, or even genuinely permissible actions; their actions are always either obligatory or recommended, done as acts of worship. He argues that since even some saints (awliyā') achieve this station, it is even more fitting for the elite of Allah's creation, i.e., the prophets.

Key Terms
كراهة
خلاف الأولى
تشريع
قربة
واجب
مندوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that actions like urinating standing are merely permissible for the Prophet, showing he was subject to ordinary rulings.
Correction: Such actions are actually obligatory for the Prophet because they serve as legislation (tashrīʿ) or to demonstrate permissibility, thus they are not neutral but have a higher purpose.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why did the Prophet perform actions like urinating standing or wudu once?
A) Because they are permissible
B) For legislation and to demonstrate permissibility
C) Because he was forgetful
D) To show that he is human

Key Takeaway
The actions of prophets, though they may appear neutral, are always either obligatory or recommended due to their legislative role and high station.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The lesson asserts that every action of the Prophet was either obligatory or recommended, never neutral. Consider your own actions today: how many were done solely with the intention of drawing closer to Allah, and how many did you treat as 'just something I do'? Can you identify one 'neutral' habit you can transform into an act of ‘ibādah by renewing your intention?
?
If even the Prophet—the most beloved to Allah—performed actions like urinating standing or washing once for wudu as acts of legislation and worship, what does that say about your own excuses for neglecting the quality of your deeds? Are you willing to re-evaluate an action you previously dismissed as 'no big deal' and seek its deeper purpose?
?
The passage uses the example of saints (awliyā’) to argue that prophets must be even more elevated. How does this make you feel about your own spiritual aspirations? Do you truly believe that you can reach a state where your actions are never neutral, or do you settle for a life of permissible distractions? What is one step you can take today to align more of your actions with the prophetic model of intentional worship?

Prophets' Actions: Only Wajib and Mandub
Al-Bajuri explains that prophets' actions are only wajib or mandub.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets' actions are confined to the obligatory and recommended, and how acts that appear permissible or disliked actually serve a higher purpose.

Core Idea
Everything a prophet does is either obligatory or a form of worship.

Al-Bajuri tackles a common question: if prophets did things like urinating standing or repeating wudu, doesn't that show they performed permissible or disliked acts? He explains that every such action was either for legislation (tashrīʿ) or to demonstrate permissibility, making it obligatory for them. This lesson establishes that prophets are free from mere permissible or disliked acts, as even saints sometimes attain such a state.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
2
Identify the objection
Look for the objection: the examples of the Prophet urinating standing or performing wudu once/twice, which might be seen as permissible or disliked.
The objection is implied in the passage; al-Bajuri directly answers it.
3
Understand the answer
Notice how al-Bajuri explains that these acts are for legislation or to show permissibility, making them obligatory for the Prophet.
He also adds that no act of a prophet is merely permissible or disliked as such.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Al-Bajuri concludes that prophets' actions are only wajib or mandub, and argues that if saints can have this state, prophets are more entitled to it.
This reinforces the special status of prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: أَوْ كَرَاهَةِ المراد بها ما يشمل خِلَافَ الأولى. ولا يَردُ على ذلك: أنه بَالَ قائماً، وتوضأ مرَّةً مرَّةً، وتوضأ مرَّتين مرَّتين؛ لأنه للتشريع ولبيان الجواز، وذلك واجب في حقه، فعلم مما تقرر أنه لا يَقَعُ منهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام محرَّم ولا مكروه على وجه كونه مكروهاً، وكذا لا يقع منهم مُبَاحٌ على وجه كونه مباحاً، بل على وجه كونه قُرْبَةً، أو للتشريع، أو للتقوي على العبادات، أو نحو ذلك، فأفعالهم دائرة بين الواجب والمندوب فقط، كيف وقد يتَّفِقُ ذلك لبعض أوليائه، فبالأولى أن يكون لصفوة الله من خلقه.)
(His saying: 'or karāha' meaning what includes khilāf al-ūlā. And it is not objected against that: that he urinated standing, and performed wudu once, and performed wudu twice; because it is for legislation and to show permissibility, and that is obligatory upon him. So it is known from what is established that there does not occur from them, peace be upon them, anything forbidden nor anything disliked as being disliked, and likewise there does not occur from them anything permissible as being permissible, but rather as being an act of worship, or for legislation, or to strengthen for acts of worship, or something like that. Thus their actions are limited to the obligatory and the recommended only. How can it be that this (permissibility) is sometimes agreed for some of His saints, then it is more fitting for the elite of Allah from His creation.)
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is a commentary by al-Bajuri on Sanusi's statement regarding the ruling of actions that are disliked (karāha) used broadly to include what is contrary to the better choice (khilāf al-ūlā). Al-Bajuri then addresses an objection: if prophets perform actions like urinating standing or performing wudu once or twice, these are sometimes considered permissible or even disliked, so how can it be said that prophets only do what is obligatory or recommended? He answers that these acts are either for legislation (tashrīʿ) or to demonstrate permissibility (bayān al-jawāz), and that is obligatory upon them. Therefore, no act of a prophet is forbidden (ḥarām) or disliked (makrūh) as such, nor is it merely permissible (mubāḥ) as such. Rather, every act is either an act of worship (qurba) or for a higher purpose like legislation or strengthening the body for worship. Hence their actions are confined to the obligatory (wājib) and the recommended (mandūb) only. Al-Bajuri supports this by arguing that if even some saints (awliyā') attain such a state, then it is even more true for the elite of Allah's creation, i.e., the prophets.

Key Terms
واجب
مندوب
مباح
مكروه
تشريع
قربة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that prophets can perform acts that are merely permissible (mubāḥ) or disliked (makrūh) as such.
Correction: Al-Bajuri clarifies that any act of a prophet is either obligatory or recommended, because even seemingly mundane acts are done for a higher purpose like legislation or worship.

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri, why do prophets perform acts like urinating standing or performing wudu multiple times?
A) Because these acts are permissible for them.
B) For legislation and to show permissibility, which is obligatory upon them.
C) Because they are following the custom of their people.
D) To demonstrate that such acts are disliked.

Key Takeaway
Prophets' actions are exclusively obligatory or recommended; any action that seems permissible or disliked actually serves a higher purpose like legislation or worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet ﷺ transformed even his most mundane acts, like urinating and performing wudu, into acts of worship and legislation. When you look at your daily routine—your eating, sleeping, speaking—how many of those actions are done with the conscious intention of drawing closer to Allah? Are you content with the gap between the Prophet’s example and your own reality? What concrete intention will you set for one ordinary action today to make it an act of worship?
?
If even the Prophet’s actions that appear ‘less than perfect’ (like urinating standing) were actually obligatory for a greater good, what does that imply about your own excuses for negligence or shortcuts in worship? Can you honestly say you never let comfort or habit override what is pleasing to Allah? Which specific area of your life requires repentance and a renewed intention to align with prophetic standards?
?
The passage argues that prophets are the ‘elite of Allah’s creation’—their every action is either obligatory or recommended. Meanwhile, your actions are often a mix of permissible, heedless, or even sinful. What is the first step you will take today to elevate one permissible habit into an act of devotion, not merely out of routine but with the awareness that you are following the prophetic model?

Prophetic Forgetfulness: Spiritual Absorption, Not Error
Al-Bajuri and al-Ajhuri explain prophetic infallibility in tabligh and in speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how prophetic forgetfulness in prayer does not contradict infallibility in conveying the message, and how the Prophet's statement about forgetting is interpreted truthfully.

Core Idea
Prophetic forgetfulness is from spiritual absorption, not from error.

This lesson explores the subtle doctrine of prophetic infallibility regarding forgetfulness. Al-Bajuri explains that while prophets cannot forget anything they are commanded to convey, they may forget in other matters, as the Prophet did in prayer due to profound awe of Allah. Al-Ajhuri then clarifies a potential misunderstanding about the Prophet's response to being asked about his forgetfulness, ensuring no imputation of falsehood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the shift from al-Bajuri's commentary to al-Ajhuri's marginal note.
2
Identify the two distinctions
Find where al-Bajuri distinguishes forgetfulness in conveying the message (not allowed) from forgetfulness in other matters (allowed, as in prayer). Also note how al-Ajhuri interprets the Prophet's reply to avoid falsehood.
The poetry line illustrates the reason for forgetfulness in prayer.
3
Reflect on the resolution
Consider why the Prophet's statement 'all of that did not happen' is interpreted as 'not in my opinion.' How does this protect his truthfulness?
This shows the care scholars take to defend prophetic infallibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: وَكِتْمَانُ شَيْءٍ مِمَّا أُمِرُوا بِتَبليغه) أي: ولو سهواً؛ لأن السهو لا يجوز عليهم في الأحكام التي يبلغونها عن الله تعالى؛ وإن جاز عليهم في غيرها، فقد سَهَا في الصلاة، لكن باشتغال قلبه بتعظيم الله تعالى، وإلى هذا المعنى أشار بعضهم بقوله: يَا سَائِلِي عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ كَيْفَ سَهَا وَالسَّهْرُ مِنْ كُلِّ قَلْبِ غَافِلِ لَاهِي قَد غَابَ عَنْ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ سِرُّهُ فَسَهَا عَمَّا سِوَى اللهِ فَالتَّعْظِيمُ. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري: الصلاة أم نسيت يا رسول الله؟ كل ذلك لم يكن، فإن هذا يوهم الكذب في الظاهر، فإن بعض الأمرين وهو النسيان قد كان، فيؤول ذلك على معنى كل ذلك لم يكن في ظني، وهذا صدق
(His saying: 'and concealing anything of what they were commanded to convey') meaning: even forgetfully; because forgetfulness is not permissible for them regarding the rulings which they convey from Allah Almighty, although it may be permissible for them in other matters. For he (the Prophet) forgot in the prayer, but due to his heart being occupied with magnifying Allah Almighty. And this meaning was indicated by some of them in his saying: 'O asker about the Messenger of Allah, how did he forget? While vigilance is from every heedless, distracted heart. He was absent from everything (due to absorption in) His secret, so he forgot what is other than Allah, out of magnification.' Marginal note of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri: 'The prayer? Did you forget, O Messenger of Allah? All of that did not happen.' For this suggests falsehood in appearance, but some of the two matters—and it is forgetfulness—did occur, so it is interpreted as meaning 'all of that did not happen in my opinion,' and this is truthful.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage combines two commentaries on prophetic infallibility. First, al-Bajuri comments on Sanusi's statement that prophets cannot conceal anything they are commanded to convey, even forgetfully. Forgetfulness (sahw) is not allowed for them regarding the rulings they convey from Allah, though it is allowed in other matters. For example, the Prophet forgot in the prayer, but this forgetfulness was due to his heart being completely absorbed in magnifying Allah, not due to negligence. Al-Bajuri cites a poetic line explaining that the Prophet's forgetfulness of worldly matters is a result of his total focus on Allah. Then, the marginal note by al-Ajhuri addresses an apparent issue: if someone asked the Prophet 'Did you forget the prayer?' and he replied 'All of that did not happen,' this might seem to imply lying because forgetfulness did occur. Al-Ajhuri resolves this by interpreting the Prophet's statement as 'all of that did not happen in my opinion (or estimation),' which is truthful because the Prophet did not perceive himself as having forgotten in that manner. This protects the Prophet from the imputation of falsehood.

Key Terms
كتمان
سهو
عصمة
تبليغ
تعظيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophetic forgetfulness in prayer contradicts infallibility.
Correction: Forgetfulness in prayer is due to spiritual absorption in Allah, not error or negligence, and does not affect infallibility in conveying the message.

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri, why is forgetfulness in conveying the message not permissible for prophets?
A) Because they are divinely protected from all forgetfulness.
B) Because it would lead to error in the law.
C) Because they are commanded to be vigilant.
D) Because forgetfulness is only allowed in worldly matters.

Key Takeaway
Prophets are infallible in conveying revelation, and any forgetfulness in other matters is due to their profound absorption in Allah, not error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are in prayer, is your forgetfulness of worldly matters due to genuine absorption in Allah's greatness, or is it simply distraction? How can you tell the difference, and what would it take to shift your heart from distraction to true ta'dhim?
?
This lesson teaches that the Prophet's forgetfulness was a sign of his profound focus on Allah. In contrast, your forgetfulness might reveal something else—what does your forgetfulness (of Allah, of your duties, of others) say about the state of your heart? Will you let it convict you to change?
?
If someone falsely accused you of something, would you be willing to defend yourself with a truthful but nuanced statement like the Prophet's 'all of that did not happen in my estimation'? Or would pride or anger push you to defend yourself in a way that compromises honesty? What does your typical response reveal about your character?

Prophets Must Have Human Attributes, Not Angelic
Al-Bajuri explains that prophets must have human attributes, not angelic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets must have human attributes and not angelic ones, and how this refutes objections to prophethood.

Core Idea
Prophets are fully human, not angels—their humanity is essential for their message.

Al-Bajuri explains a key attribute of prophets: they must be human, not angelic. This might seem obvious, but some early opponents of Islam denied prophethood because they expected a messenger to be an angel. Al-Bajuri clarifies the rational basis for prophethood requiring human attributes, using a Quranic verse as evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice how al-Bajuri defines 'bashariyya' and then contrasts it with angelic attributes.
2
Understand the term 'bashariyya'
Al-Bajuri explains that 'bashar' (human) is derived from 'bashara' (skin). This connects to the visible human form. The restriction to human attributes excludes angelic ones.
3
Identify the refuted claim
The ignorant Arabs argued that a messenger should have angelic attributes like not eating or drinking. Al-Bajuri rejects this, affirming that prophets must have human needs.
4
Connect to the Quranic verse
Al-Bajuri cites Quran 25:7, where the disbelievers question the Prophet's humanity. This verse is used to validate the necessity of human attributes.
Reflect on why this objection was raised and how Islam responds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: الْبَشَرِيَّةِ) أي: المتعلّقة بالبشر، وهم بنو آدم سموا بذلك؛ لبُدُو بشرتهم، وهي ظاهرُ الجلد. وخرج بهذا القيد الأعراض المتعلقة بالملائكة، فلا تجوز عليهم، خلافاً لجَهَلَة العرب في زعمهم: أن الرسول يكون متّصفاً بصفات الملائكة، فلا يأكل ولا يشرب، وتوصلوا بذلك إلى نفي رسالته كما حكاه الله تعالى عنهم في قوله: وَقَالُواْ مَالِ هَذَا الرَّسُولِ يَأْكُلُ الطَّعَامَ وَيَمْشِي فِي الْأَسْوَاقِ الآية.
(His saying: 'al-bashariyya') meaning: related to humans, and they are the sons of Adam, so called because of the appearance of their skin (bashara), which is the outer layer of skin. And by this restriction, the accidents related to angels are excluded, so they are not permissible for them (the prophets), contrary to the ignorant Arabs in their claim that the messenger should be characterized by the attributes of angels, so he neither eats nor drinks, and they used that to deny his message, as Allah Almighty narrated about them in His saying: 'And they said: What is this messenger who eats food and walks in the markets?' [Al-Furqan: 7]
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a commentary by al-Bajuri on Sanusi's term 'al-bashariyya' (humanity). Al-Bajuri explains that 'human' (bashar) refers to the children of Adam, named for their skin (bashara). The restriction to human accidents (a'rāḍ) excludes those accidents that are specific to angels. Therefore, prophets cannot have angelic attributes such as not eating or drinking. This refutes the ignorant Arabs who argued that a true messenger should be like an angel, without human needs, and used this to deny the prophethood of Muhammad. Al-Bajuri cites the Quranic verse (25:7) where the disbelievers question: 'What is this messenger who eats food and walks in the markets?' implying that being human contradicts prophethood in their view. Al-Bajuri affirms that prophets must be human and possess human attributes.

Key Terms
بشرية
أعراض
ملائكة
أكل
شرب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets should be angels who do not eat or drink.
Correction: Prophets must be human with human needs; angelic attributes are not permissible for them.

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri, why must prophets possess human attributes like eating and drinking?
A) Because they are commanded to do so.
B) Because accidents related to angels are not permissible for them.
C) Because it is better for them to be humble.
D) Because they are not angels.

Key Takeaway
Prophets must be human with human attributes, and this is essential for their role as messengers to humanity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel weak or hungry, do you ever see that as a flaw in your spiritual state? How does knowing that the Prophet also felt hunger and thirst change your view of your own humanity?
?
The ignorant Arabs rejected the Prophet because he walked in the markets and ate food. Are there ways you unconsciously expect religious leaders to be 'superhuman' and free from ordinary needs? Where does that expectation come from, and how can you realign it with the truth of this lesson?
?
If you were to meet the Prophet Muhammad today and saw him eating or sleeping, would that diminish his status in your eyes? What does your answer reveal about your understanding of prophecy? Commit to one practical change in how you relate to human weakness, based on this lesson.

Prophets: No Concealment, But Allowed Forgetfulness
Al-Bajuri explains the prohibition of concealment and the allowance of forgetfulness for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets must convey all revelation without concealment—even unintentionally—and that forgetfulness in non-conveyance matters is permissible and attributed to profound reverence.

Core Idea
Prophets never conceal revelation; their forgetfulness stems from awe, not neglect.

Al-Bajuri clarifies a subtle condition of prophethood: the absolute prohibition of concealing any part of revelation, whether intentional or not. He then addresses an apparent contradiction—how can prophets forget in worldly matters? The answer lies in the depth of their devotion. Let's explore this foundational doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Notice the key terms كتمان and سهو.
The passage includes a poetic couplet and a marginal note—these are part of the explanation.
2
Understand the distinction
Notice how forgetfulness is forbidden when conveying divine rulings but allowed in other matters. Ask: why would this distinction exist?
The distinction preserves the trustworthiness of revelation while acknowledging human nature.
3
Reflect on the example
The Prophet's forgetfulness in prayer is explained as a result of his heart being occupied with glorifying Allah. Consider how this transforms the understanding of forgetfulness from a flaw to a sign of devotion.
The poetic couplet reinforces this idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: وَكِتْمَانُ شَيْءٍ مِمَّا أُمِرُوا بِتَبليغه) أي: ولو سهواً؛ لأن السهو لا يجوز عليهم في الأحكام التي يبلغونها عن الله تعالى؛ وإن جاز عليهم في غيرها، فقد سَهَا في الصلاة، لكن باشتغال قلبه بتعظيم الله تعالى، وإلى هذا المعنى أشار بعضهم بقوله:
يَا سَائِلِي عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ كَيْفَ سَهَا وَالسَّهْرُ مِنْ كُلِّ قَلْبِ غَافِلِ لَاهِي
الله
قَد غَابَ عَنْ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ سِرُّهُ فَسَهَا عَمَّا سِوَى اللهِ فَالتَّعْظِيمُ

حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري
(قوله: قَدْ غَابَ هذا جواب السؤال.
:(وقوله: عَنْ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ ومنه الصلاة، والمراد بالسر القلب.
His saying: 'And concealing something of what they were commanded to convey' means: even if unintentionally, because forgetfulness is not permissible for them regarding the rulings they convey from Allah the Exalted, though it is permissible for them in other matters. He (the Prophet) forgot in prayer, but due to his heart being occupied with glorifying Allah the Exalted. To this meaning some alluded by his saying: 'O my questioner about the Messenger of Allah, how did he forget, while vigilance is from every heedless and playful heart? Allah. He was absent from everything in secret, so he forgot what is other than Allah, thus glorification.'
Marginal note of al-Allama Ahmad al-Ajhuri: His saying: 'He was absent' – this is the answer to the question. And his saying: 'from everything' includes prayer, and the intended meaning of 'secret' is the heart.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage defines and explains one of the conditions of prophethood: the obligation of conveying revelation and the impermissibility of concealing any part of it, even unintentionally. Al-Bajuri clarifies that forgetfulness (sahw) is not allowed for prophets concerning the divine rulings they are commanded to transmit, but it is allowed in worldly matters or acts of worship not related to conveying. He cites the incident of the Prophet's forgetfulness in prayer as evidence, explaining that it was due to his heart being absorbed in the veneration of Allah. A couplet is quoted to illustrate that such forgetfulness stems from profound reverence, not negligence. The marginal note by al-Ajhuri clarifies the line 'He was absent from everything' as the answer to the rhetorical question, and interprets 'everything' as including even prayer, with 'secret' meaning the heart.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets cannot forget anything at all.
Correction: This passage shows that prophets can forget in matters unrelated to conveying revelation, as seen in the Prophet's forgetfulness in prayer due to his heart being absorbed in glorifying Allah.

Checkpoint

A) Because he was distracted by worldly affairs.

C) Because he was not infallible in prayer.
D) Because he was tired from conveying revelation.

Key Takeaway
Prophets must never conceal any part of revelation, even by mistake, and their forgetfulness in other matters stems from intense reverence for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you catch yourself distracted in prayer, do you attribute it to forgetfulness rooted in worldly concerns, or do you ever consider it a sign that your heart is truly absorbed in Allah? Which possibility aligns with the prophetic example in this lesson, and how can you cultivate the latter?
?
The Prophet's heart was so filled with the awe of Allah that he forgot everything else. Is there a single moment in your day when your awareness of Allah's greatness similarly overshadows all other thoughts? What would need to change for such moments to become more frequent?
?
Prophets never concealed any part of the message, even when it was difficult. Is there a truth you know—about yourself, about your faith, about justice—that you are afraid to speak or act upon? What would it cost you to stop concealing it, and are you willing to pay that price?
